Sudden Increase in Japanese Troops in Malanyu

Hotels and Restaurants in the Town are Almost Entirely Occupied - Many Japanese Planes Fly in from Jinzhou - Wang Zhanshan's Security Team Opens in Jixian from Sanhe 4

(Tianjin) Four Japanese planes flew from Chengde to Malanyu on the 19th and landed at the local airfield. In addition, more than 300 Japanese troops arrived in the area from Jinzhou. All the hotels and restaurants in the town were occupied, and some who could not find accommodation went to Saheqiao to temporarily reside. Japanese troops are stationed in the Malanyu long-distance telephone and telegraph bureau to handle military communications. The military long-distance telephone line built by the Japanese troops between Malanyu and Saheqiao has been completed and was tested on the 18th.

(20th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Japanese troops in Jixian began withdrawing to Malanyu yesterday morning, divided into two batches. The first batch of more than 150 people, led by a lieutenant, withdrew at 6:00 a.m. yesterday. The remaining 50, led personally by Hayashida, completed their withdrawal at 2:00 p.m. yesterday afternoon. The security team under Wang Zhanyuan has arrived in Jixian from Sanhe. (20th Special Dispatch)

They are conducting various combat exercises day and night. (20th Central News Agency Telegram)

(Beiping) The issue of the passes on the Great Wall that have not been taken over was raised for consultation at the Yuguan meeting this time. Malanyu is expected to be taken over next month. Matsui is scheduled to fly from Chengde to Changchun on the 27th of this month to discuss the matter with the headquarters of the Kwantung Army. The remaining passes, such as Jieling, Lengkou, Yiyuan, and Xifeng, are all stationed with Japanese troops and puppet police and gendarmerie, making a solution difficult. It has been agreed that the puppet police in Gubeikou will withdraw from the first of next month. The withdrawal point for the puppet police is in Bashikaying, which is in the boundary of Luanping County. The Japanese troops in Gubeikou have decided not to move. The Japanese troops in Saheqiao in Xifengkou have recently been building barracks, intending to stay for a long time. The entrance of Xifengkou is equipped with a puppet police station, and the director is a Japanese named Harada Yuichi, who is very strict in inspecting travelers. (20th Special Dispatch)

Yu Xuezhong Talks About the Special Police Problem in the War Zone 5

(Tianjin) Yu Xuezhong told reporters that the newly formed special police in the war zone, according to the Tanggu Agreement, were originally to number 9,000, but we have now formed 8,000, with 5,000 rifles, divided into two general brigades. The first brigade leader is Zhang Qingyu, currently stationed in Cangxian, and the second brigade leader is Zhang Yantian, currently stationed in Caicun. The general brigade is divided into eight districts, and the detachments will be

stationed in the Luanyu and Jimin districts to maintain order. In addition to the Ye Lei and Liu Zuo Zhou units, the remaining units of Wei Yonghe, Zhou Yuying, and Dou Xizhe are all being transferred back for rest. However, during the rotation, it is feared that bandits will take the opportunity to cause trouble, so the various disputes in the war zone must first be resolved with the Japanese side before implementation can be carried out. As for the Jixian dispute, the Japanese side was initially extremely rude, intending to confiscate the light and heavy machine guns of our militia security team. After Commissioner Yin's negotiations, it has now been resolved. As for the abolition of excessive levies, it should be handled urgently, but it can only be maintained if there are compensation measures, otherwise, all administrative affairs will have to be completely suspended. Reports that Hebei Province has as many as 300 kinds of excessive levies are somewhat exaggerated. In reality, there are only dozens. If the central government can provide subsidies for political expenses, it can be completely abolished. (20th Central News Agency Dispatch) (Beiping) The newly trained security team in the war zone has completed its training and, after negotiations with the Japanese side, is scheduled to move to the war zone for rotation on July 1. It is divided into two large brigades, the first brigade, Zhang Qingyu's unit, stationed in the Luanyu district, and the second brigade, Zhang Yantian's unit, stationed in the Jimin district. The original security teams of Dou Xizhe, Wei Yonghe, Zhou Yuying, etc., are all transferred back for training. Zhao Lei and Liu Zuozhou will remain in Luandong, defending the original positions. (20th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Qin Fen Talks About League of Nations Technical Cooperation 6

(Nanjing) Qin Fen, Secretary of the Economic Council, recently returned to Nanjing after being summoned to Jiangxi by Chairman Chiang to discuss various tasks in the recovered bandit areas. He stated that the League of Nations' technical cooperation with China only involves sending experts to provide technical guidance, so the League of Nations Advisory Committee accepted Lehman's recommendation to send several more technical experts to China to assist the Construction Commission. China will send personnel to foreign countries to carefully study all practical technologies. In addition, there is no other assistance of any other nature. At present, China must also redouble its efforts to break through difficulties, and there is no need to completely rely on others. Regarding the League of Nations' discussion of China's technical problems, all details have been reported to the central government by Representative Gu by telegram, and the content is roughly the same as that reported in various newspapers. As for the term of office of advisor Lehman, it expires in September of this year. Whether he will return to China to work again will be decided by the League of Nations. Regarding the Northwest Development Plan, after Standing Committee Member Song's inspection of various provinces in the Northwest, the completion of highways and water conservancy in various provinces in the Northwest will be completed. Song and the chairmen of various provinces in the Northwest have a concrete decision. After Song enters Beijing, a full standing committee meeting will be convened to discuss other undertakings to develop the Northwest. (20th Special Dispatch)

Misinterpretation of the Nine-Power Treaty

British Foreign Secretary's Remarks Cause Repercussions - US Sees as Unfortunate as Previous Remarks Recognizing Japanese Privileges - Shi Makes Statement That Treaty Signatory Countries Should Bear Dual Obligations 8

(London) The Washington dispatch of the London Observer regarding Chinese affairs stated that the British Foreign Secretary Simon's remarks yesterday regarding not being responsible for the integrity of the Nine-Power Treaty are considered as unfortunate as the British Foreign Secretary's previous remarks recognizing Japan's special rights in China. If Japan disregards this treaty and frustrates the principle of open door, there is nothing to be done, as the United States cannot maintain it alone, nor may it be willing to maintain it jointly with other countries. However, the United States still relies on Britain's diplomatic assistance as the best way to prevent China from being slaughtered. This is why Secretary of State John Hay made the declaration to maintain China's open door. (20th Reuters Dispatch)

(Washington) When British Foreign Secretary Simon answered a question from Labor Party member Clipper in the House of Commons on the 18th of this month regarding the Sino-Japanese issue, he stated that the Washington Nine-Power Treaty only stated that the signatory countries should respect China's political independence and territorial integrity, and there was no provision for maintaining China's independence and integrity by force. Recently, Shi Zhaoji, the Chinese ambassador to the United States, issued a statement stating that Foreign Secretary Simon's words are only partially true. Because China is a member of the League of Nations, and the Treaty of Peace to which the League of Nations Covenant belongs, Britain is also one of the signatories. According to Article 10 of the Covenant, member states should not only respect the territorial integrity and political independence of other member states, but also have a joint obligation to maintain them and prevent foreign aggression. (19th Havas Dispatch)

Huang Fu's Representative Arrives in Beiping

Discusses Transportation Problems with Yin - Tianjin Telegram Transmits That Yin Has Been Summoned South 9

(Beiping) Huang Fu's representative Xu Xiuzhi arrived in Beiping from Shanghai this morning. After Xu got off the train, he boarded Yin Tong's private car and went straight to Yin's residence. Huang will return to Beiping early next month after the issue of postal and transportation links is resolved. The plan for traffic between Ping and Shen, which Yin Tong and Ota discussed at the Yuguan meeting before, has been sent to Huang for review. It will be submitted to the central government for review and modification before it can become a final decision. When Yin Tong and Ota discussed the plan proposed at Yuguan this time, they originally agreed to reply before the end of May. It is reported that Huang is in Shanghai and the deadline of the end of May is approaching, so he specially sent representative Xu Xiuzhi north again to negotiate with Yin Tong and others to review the original draft as soon as possible and then submit it to the central government for approval. (20th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) In the afternoon of the 20th, Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, was summoned by telegram from the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Railways to leave Beiping and go south to Beijing. Zheng Baozhao, the Deputy Director of the road, is still in Beidaihe. Japanese Return Private Property in the Northeast - Organize Industrial Trust Company - Handle Registration and Extract Commission - Only Zhang Xueliang and Feng Yong Excepted 11

(Beiping) Northeast people who fled into the Customs after the September 18th Incident either did not dare to return to their hometowns to manage their property due to fear of the Japanese, or were not allowed. For years, everything has been in the hands of the Japanese. The Japanese, in order to win over certain figures, instructed relevant parties that, with the exception of the property of Zhang Xueliang and Feng Yong, which is absolutely confiscated, the remainder can be returned. Therefore, Cao and Lu, four key figures of a certain faction, who are currently residing in Tianjin, organized the Manchurian Industrial Trust Company in the Japanese concession of Tianjin to handle this matter. Since its establishment, it has been three months, and the commission has earned more than one million yuan. The method is to extract a commission of 200 yuan for every 10,000 yuan, and then the company pays a tax of 100 yuan to the puppet government. After hearing the news, Northeast people in the Customs have approached the company for assistance. It is said that most of the property of well-known Northeast people has been returned as requested. However, in the divorce case between Feng Yong and his wife Jiang Jintao, the judgment ordered Feng to pay Jiang over 500 hectares of land near the Beida Camp and several pawnshops. The puppet government has approved Jiang to receive them. In addition, due to the fact that Feng owned all the assets, they were priced and auctioned. (20th Special Dispatch)

Current Commentary

National Financial Conference Opens 12

— English Translation

The long-awaited National Financial Conference opened today in Nanjing. In addition to key officials from the Ministry of Finance and responsible officials for finance from various provinces and cities, many experts with social reputation are also participating. Bringing together the government and the public to discuss reforms to the national budget and offer strategies. Gathering ideas from various sources, how can it not be called a major event today? However, considering the current situation, we must urgently make great efforts. We still remember that the first National Financial Conference was convened in July of the 17th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1928]. At that time, the National Government had overthrown the Northern Warlords and began a movement to rejuvenate the country with the people. Therefore, it intended to end the chaotic wartime finance and establish a national finance that develops production. Considering what the government publicized at that time and what the public opinion expressed, we could not help but think that the future was bright. However, time flies, and six years have passed. Now, we hear about the convening of the second conference. The purpose of the conference, besides streamlining tax revenue and adjusting expenditures, does not seem to include any further renewal plans. Today, various undertakings are riddled with problems. Even if the financial authorities are as diligent as Li Xian [a famous Tang Dynasty chancellor known for his diligence], they may still sigh that they have the will but lack the strength. This conference stems from the motivation to strive for prosperity and vigorously advance, which is acknowledged by the people of the country. However, whether it can avoid repeating the mistakes of the past cannot be determined by the conference itself. May I point out three of the biggest problems with our national finance? First, the unreasonable expansion of expenditures. According to the central budget expenditures, during the Beijing government era, it never exceeded 500 million yuan per year. After the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, expenditures expanded without limit, but the funding for production and construction has not increased. Taking the current year as an example, the budgeted expenditure has reached a huge sum of 828,921,964 yuan, and military spending alone accounts for 415,600,000 yuan. In addition, the actual expenditures not included in the report may be even more than this amount.

Second, the shrinking of regular revenue. Currently, the central government's revenue still relies heavily on customs and salt taxes. Customs and salt taxes are commodity taxes. Compared with the United States and the United Kingdom, where people's income tax is the main source of revenue, the advantages and disadvantages are vastly different. In recent years, commerce has been sluggish, and industry and commerce have declined. After the loss of the Northeast, the source of tax revenue has been greatly reduced. As a result, the central government's regular revenue has been severely hit. Attempts to cut spending have failed, and instead, efforts are being made to increase revenue. The issuance of public bonds has accumulated over time, and special tax revenue is not easy to quickly eliminate. Recently, former Finance Minister Song Ziwen, upon returning from the Northwest, said that special taxes "are difficult to replace, ultimately making it difficult to enforce the ban on opium." These are truly heartfelt words.

Third, the corruption of the tax system. Our country's tax system has been corrupt for a long time. The National Government has repeatedly regarded reforming the tax system as one of the key aspects of striving for prosperity. However, over the years, old taxes have not been reduced, and new levies have become increasingly dense. The central government's decrees are like mountains, while the local officials treat them like worn-out shoes. As a result, goods cannot circulate, and production cannot develop, all because of the corruption of the tax system. Our country failed to actively establish and implement a refreshing financial policy in the situation of the first financial conference, deeply regretting the missed opportunity. Now, the slump in commerce is even worse, and international aggression is even greater. Whether the above three problems will worsen or improve depends entirely on future efforts. I sincerely hope that all those attending the financial conference can identify these three issues as targets, formulate concrete and feasible remedial plans, and seek practical application rather than pleasing theoretical solutions. This will be fulfilling your duties to the fullest. As for whether it can be fully implemented, it depends on the determination and perseverance of those who implement it in the future.

Hirota and Ariyoshi Agree

New Policy Towards China, Opposing Interference in Chinese Affairs by Third Countries, Advocating Friendship to Induce Us to Resolve Pending Issues 13

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota hosted a luncheon on the 19th for Ambassador to China Ariyoshi, who is returning to his post on the evening of the 23rd, as well as Vice Minister Shigemitsu, and Directors-General and Department Heads such as Kurasu, Togo, and Amau. They exchanged views on Japan's policy towards China, and as a result, the following policies were decided:

(1) The Japanese government and China jointly assume responsibility for maintaining peace and promoting prosperity in East Asia, and reject all actions by third countries that interfere or use the name of cooperation with China to engage in political means.

(2) Resolving pending issues between China and Japan is a prerequisite for establishing Sino-Japanese friendship and establishing peace in East Asia. If China is sincere, Japan will not hesitate to provide any effort to help resolve pending issues.

(3) The Japanese government will always provide well-intentioned guidance to China's requests, avoid local negotiations, and assist the Chinese government in order to restore its prosperity and unification. (Jiji News Agency dispatch, 20th)

Communist Forces Lurk in Japanese Army and Navy 14

(Tokyo) According to a statement by the Ministry of the Army, between November of the 7th year of Showa (i.e., 1932) and October of the 8th year of Showa, 121 communists were discovered within the Japanese army, including 12 officers, 3 non-commissioned officers, and 106 soldiers. In addition, the Ministry of the Navy has separately discovered 5 communists. (China United News dispatch, 20th)

Former US Secretary of War Observes That a World War Is Inevitable, American Involvement in International Peace Efforts Could Save the Dangerous Situation 15

(New York) According to the opinion of former Secretary of War Baker, if countries continue to compete in armaments, a second world war is inevitable. However, Baker also stated that if the United States cooperates with other countries to maintain international peace, it can still be salvaged. More than ten organizations promoting international peace have distributed petitions throughout the United States. Baker expressed his opinion on this, and the petition seeks national opinions on the United States formally joining the League of Nations. Baker's declaration stated, "There is no doubt that countries around the world are rapidly falling into an arms race. If this trend continues, a second tragic world war will be the inevitable result. Politicians can only say and do what their national public opinion and wishes dictate. Therefore, a formal collection of opinions, such as that initiated by the League of Nations Association, is essential. The League of Nations Association advocates that the United States declare the conditions for its accession to the League of Nations, so that the government of our country, representing a vast land and a large population, can fully understand the will of the people and act accordingly. The forces of law, justice, and peace throughout the world are now fighting against the forces of suspicion, fear, and aggression. Therefore, if the United States can express its cooperation as soon as possible, it may be able to avert the dangerous situation." (National News dispatch, 19th)

Due to the Arms Embargo Issue

American Sanctions Theory Revived, Washington Awaits for All Countries to Express Their Intentions, Hoping That Words and Actions Match to Achieve Practical Results 16

(London) A Washington dispatch from the London Observer states that the wave of calls for a European arms embargo has now sparked discussions in the United States regarding sanctions. The Senate previously held a position against sanctions, but months ago, President Roosevelt expressed his opinion that the United States should join European powers in supporting sanctions, and the Senate changed its attitude. Now, due to the arms embargo issue, sanctions discussions have been revived. Statistics on US Arms Exports to China The statistics on US arms exports have recently been released. Exports to China in the first three months of this year totaled US$1.1 million, mostly aircraft engines and parts. In addition, excellent American technicians, pilots, and powerful salesmen have gone to China. Therefore, those discussing arms embargoes are now paying attention to this statistic. It is expected that the Senate will handle this matter after research. (Reuters dispatch, 20th)

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull stated today that the US government has consulted with major countries on the issue of an arms embargo on Bolivia and Paraguay. Hull declared that the US has taken the lead in controlling the international arms trade, and is now awaiting the participation of other governments before taking further action. Hull hopes that other countries that have sold arms to Bolivia and Paraguay will be consistent in their words and actions and implement the highly touted arms embargo to achieve practical results. He is currently awaiting replies from various countries explaining their policies and intentions, paying more attention to the replies from countries such as Argentina, Brazil, Chile, and Peru. Hull currently does not want to announce which governments he has contacted or from which countries he has received replies. The government is also using a special Senate investigating committee to thoroughly investigate American arms companies, paying particular attention to international conspiracies among major companies to create war rumors and incite arms races. The first to be investigated are domestic arms manufacturers, bankers, merchants, chemical plants, and schemes and profiteering plots between aircraft and shipbuilding plants. Secondly, it will investigate in detail the collusion between these companies and major European arms dealers, and their activities in South America, China, and Japan. The scope of this investigation is as broad as the situation caused by the recent European espionage case. The Senate's secret investigators have been granted the power to act as appropriate, so that no suspected person, company, or organization is missed. These secret investigators will be busy collecting materials in the coming months and reporting to the Special Committee on Armaments. (National News dispatch, 19th)

Lafayette Centennial Memorial, US and France Connect Diplomatic Ties, US Congress Holds Solemn Commemorative Ceremony, French Authorities Express the Necessity of Maintaining Friendship in Telegraph 17

(Paris) The US Senate and House of Representatives are scheduled to hold a joint meeting today to commemorate the centennial of the death of French General Lafayette, who helped the US achieve independence. Innumerable ceremonies have been held in major American cities this year to commemorate Lafayette, but the most solemn of these is the ceremony held by the Congress today, as President Roosevelt will personally attend and deliver a speech before the authorities of each state and the diplomatic community. French Ambassador de Laboulaye will also deliver a speech. President Lebrun sent a letter to the United States on behalf of the French people, expressing friendly respect to the American people and Congress. The letter stated that the relationship between the United States and France has roots in humanitarianism and will be everlasting. General Lafayette, who is jointly commemorated today, is not only French but also an American citizen. It concluded that the alliance between France and the United States is one of the main conditions for maintaining world peace, and that the two countries should adopt paths that love peace and respect personality in order to continue to seek progress and prosperity. Other important French figures, such as Foreign Minister Barthou, the speakers of the Senate and House of Representatives, and the chairmen of the foreign affairs committees of both houses, also took the opportunity to send telegrams to the speakers of the US Congress, promoting the friendship between the two countries for over a century, stating that whenever reason and justice are threatened, the two countries always unite to protect them. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Russia Denies the Dismissal of General Galen, Claims Japanese are Spreading Malicious Rumors 18

(Moscow) The Japanese news agency reported that Commander of the Far Eastern Special Red Army, Buryukhin (i.e., General Galen), had been recalled to Moscow, and that he was plotting to incite war between Japan and the Soviet Union and participating in a certain conspiracy. At the same time, his position as commander has been replaced by Yegorov. This report is purely malicious slander and provocation, and has no basis whatsoever. (Tass dispatch, 19th)

Italy and Germany Discuss Disarmament 19

Rome The German disarmament representative Ribbentrop arrived in Rome today and was received by Italian Prime Minister Mussolini to discuss disarmament issues. The discussion lasted for quite some time, and both sides agreed that it was necessary to establish a convention. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

The League of Nations Administrative Council Adjourns, Scheduled to Reconvene on May 30, Saar and Chaco Issues Pending Resolution 20

(Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council adjourned today until May 30, and the issues on the agenda have not been resolved to date. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

(Geneva) The Administrative Council passed a resolution today, scheduling an extraordinary meeting of the Administrative Council to be held on May 30 of this year to discuss the Chaco dispute, and also entrusted the three-person committee on the Chaco issue to take beneficial measures so that the British proposal to ban arms shipments to the Chaco would have a follow-up. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Telegraphing All Countries to Ban Arms Shipments 21

(Geneva) Regarding the dispute between Bolivia and Paraguay, the Administrative Council sent telegrams to the countries that recognized the ban on arms shipments to Bolivia and Paraguay last year, asking whether those countries were prepared to implement a ban on the shipment of arms, weapons, and aircraft produced in their own country to Bolivia and Paraguay, or to ban the transit of such ordnance imported from other countries to Bolivia and Paraguay. France, the United Kingdom, Italy, Germany, China, and Japan are all among those to whom telegrams were sent. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations took swift action today to prevent unnecessary sacrifices in the Chaco War between Bolivia and Paraguay. The League of Nations today telegraphed 31 countries around the world requesting them to join the arms embargo against Bolivia and Paraguay. The United Kingdom and the United States are the major countries that manufacture and export arms and weapons, and they have now taken the lead in the embargo movement and believe that it will definitely succeed. It is a historic first for all countries to act in concert to stop the war. The United Kingdom advocated this action as early as November 1932, when it negotiated with various countries in order to realize a global arms embargo. In early 1933, the League of Nations formally exchanged views with various countries, and most countries expressed their willingness to take joint action, but only if the United States, France, Italy, and Germany agreed. At that time, the United States stated that it had no authority to implement it because it had not obtained congressional approval, which led to an interruption. President Roosevelt submitted a special message to Congress on Friday, requesting immediate approval of the 1925 Geneva Convention on the Supervision and Control of the International Arms Trade, which further called for the League of Nations to take further control. Senator Pittman's bill, which specifically authorizes the government to announce an arms embargo on Bolivia and Paraguay, is expected to pass the Senate this week. (National News dispatch, 19th)

Commendation to Brazil for Mediation between Colombia and Peru 22

Geneva Regarding the dispute between Colombia and Peru, the Administrative Council reviewed the various agreements signed by the two countries in the Brazilian capital during this session, and immediately telegraphed the chairmen of the two countries' conferences, former Brazilian Foreign Minister Franco, and the authorities of Colombia and Peru, praising their efforts for peace. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Brazilian Capital, Rio de Janeiro The dispute between Peru and Colombia over the Leticia border in South America has been mediated by Brazil and has now ended. Today, Brazilian Foreign Minister Franco claimed that the warring parties have now established an agreement to end hostilities based on the methods he proposed. It is heard that after the signing of this agreement, diplomatic relations between the two countries will be restored immediately. Leticia was ceded to Colombia six years ago, but Peruvians occupied it in September 1932, causing each side to refuse to yield, leading to war in February of the following year. The League of Nations tried to mediate last June, sending an American, a Brazilian, and a Spaniard as administrative commissioners of Leticia, but the final resolution was actually facilitated by Brazil. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Rio de Janeiro (Brazil) According to reliable sources, the Colombian-Peruvian peace treaty contains a non-aggression treaty between the two countries, the designation of Leticia as a demilitarized zone, and a trade and navigation treaty between the two countries. Peru also expressed its regrets to Colombia and promised to refer future disputes to the International Court of Justice in The Hague. Leticia will temporarily belong to Colombia pending resolution through diplomatic negotiations, and in the future, Peru may exchange this area for land elsewhere. (National News dispatch, 19th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations' special committee on the Saar issue discussed the conclusions and recommendations of its work this evening, and at the suggestion of the chairman of the special committee, Italian Alaya, it was decided that "the report on the Saar region is not yet complete, and the entire issue should be further discussed at the extraordinary meeting of the Administrative Council on May 30 of this year. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

French Foreign Minister's Pre-Departure Remarks 23

(Paris) Foreign Minister Barthou and Massigli, director of the French office at the League of Nations, returned from Geneva last night and arrived here at 7:00 this morning. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

(Geneva) Regarding the Saar issue, the Administrative Council has decided to postpone the discussion until the extraordinary meeting on May 30. French Foreign Minister Barthou recently gave an interview to the French press, saying that the diplomatic negotiations this time were extremely difficult, and that some of the circumstances were contradictory. He could not tell them now, but he had always worked with a sincere spirit to ensure that France's attitude was in accordance with the peace treaty, and that France had interpreted the treaty in a fair and open manner, and that it sought to be accurate and unmistakable. He participated in the preparations for the Saar vote, and he never forgot this idea of peace. He had great faith in the efforts of the special committee on the Saar issue, and the Italian representative Alaya encouraged it with a fair attitude, which was especially unforgettable. He had made concessions on this issue, which seemed controversial, but there were still some points that he could never concede. He never retreated. For example, the date of the Saar vote could only be determined after the freedom of the voters and the safety of all residents were effectively guaranteed. He insisted on this throughout. If he had failed to demand guarantees of the freedom of voters and the safety of residents, and had proceeded to approve the date of the vote, he would have been not only a traitor to France, but also a criminal of the League of Nations, because the rights of both would have been harmed. Now that the Saar issue has been decided to be postponed for discussion, he should not say much more, because the special committee on the Saar issue is still continuing negotiations, and speaking too much may hinder the negotiations. Until the last moment, he still hoped that this meeting would be successful. Although he was unable to achieve his wish, the French delegation had nothing to hide. When the League of Nations Administrative Council reconvenes to discuss this matter, the French representatives will speak frankly about what they have seen, and the French will have no shame in the face of those in the world who are sincere and thoughtful. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Establishment of a Dictatorial Government in Bulgaria

Important International Developments in Central Europe, Bulgaria's New Diplomacy Focuses on Peace and Good Neighbor Policy, Pan-Slavic Alliance Possible 24

(London) After Bulgaria's change, there may be important international developments, as the new government will actively change Bulgaria's diplomatic policy in order to establish an alliance with Yugoslavia and pursue a pan-Slavic policy. It is heard that Macedonian leader Mihailov and many of his party members have been arrested. If this is true, then the alliance between Bulgaria and Yugoslavia will be easier to establish. (Reuters dispatch, 20th)

Sofia After the Bulgarian Prime Minister failed to organize a cabinet in the parliament, the parliament has been dissolved, and all political parties have suspended their activities. The military dictatorship was immediately established. This afternoon, Prime Minister Mushanov entered the palace to meet with King Boris to report on the failure of the organization. At the same time, the political situation took a sharp turn. King Boris ordered former Railway Minister Georgiev to form a cabinet, and at the same time gave the full power of the dictatorship to the King, and signed an edict dissolving Parliament. After receiving the order, Georgiev immediately engaged in the organization of the new cabinet. It is heard that there will be many military officers in it, such as General Vathev, who will be responsible for the Ministry of Military Affairs and Communications, and General Bogadiev, etc. Georgiev recently issued a declaration stating that the basis of the new government is the support of the army. Georgiev also announced to the people of the country that they should maintain order and wait quietly for results, and declared that the new government's foreign policy is to maintain friendly relations with neighboring countries, and other domestic affairs, such as improving the economy, eradicating communism, and abolishing the party system, etc. Sofia is still under martial law, and major streets are guarded by heavy troops, and machine guns are erected in important locations. Telephone and telegraph services are also partially suspended for inspection. However, the country is still quiet. (National News dispatch, 19th)

President Issues Four Orders, Guarding the Capital of Bulgaria 25

There have been rumors of troop movements in Bulgaria. It was not until last night that they were confirmed. Former Prime Minister Mushanov was ordered by King Boris to try to form a new cabinet, but after two days of negotiations, he resigned. Last night, the national army set out and occupied all the major strategic locations in the capital and provincial cities. The residences of former cabinet members were all guarded. Traffic in the city was completely blocked at 3:00 in the morning and entered a state of lockdown until noon. At 10:00 in the morning, King Boris signed three orders: (1) Former Prime Minister Mushanov did not need to handle routine affairs; (2) Georgiev was appointed as Prime Minister, temporarily serving as Foreign Minister; (3) Mitilev was appointed as Minister of the Interior, temporarily serving as Minister of Justice, and Todorov as Minister of Finance. It is estimated that the position of Foreign Minister will be held by Ambassador to France Batolov. In addition, the King signed an order merging the Ministry of Public Works and the Ministry of Railways into the Ministry of Communications, and merging the Ministry of Commerce, Industry, Labor, and Agriculture into the Ministry of Economy. It is difficult to determine what attitude public opinion holds towards the coup, but it is credible that most people express sympathy for the new government. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

New Government Issues Proclamation, Appeasing the People of the Capital of Bulgaria 26

The new government issued a proclamation to the people of the country, explaining the reasons for the change of government, saying that the various political groups in the country were divided, and that disputes often arose between politicians and individuals. The party system of government has completely failed, and people are panicking. Administrative facilities have lost their normal state. Under these circumstances, a stable government could not be formed, and it was imperative to organize a "nationally united" government beyond political parties. In this state of national disintegration, only the army stood independently, embracing the ambition to stop the crisis and save the country. The new government was able to accomplish its transformation because of the power of the army.

Continued Proclamation on Revamping Domestic and Foreign Policies 27

The proclamation also elaborated on the new government's policy as follows: (1) Reorganize discipline to determine national policy; (2) Merge several ministries; (3) Stabilize the positions of civil servants; (4) Restore the authority of the government; (5) Achieve a balanced budget to restore national credit; (6) Help agriculture; (7) Prevent unemployment; (8) Reorganize the judiciary. In terms of foreign policy, the new government will strive to continue good relations with all countries and restore diplomatic relations with the Soviet Union. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Cutting and Merging Central and Local Agencies, Capital of Bulgaria 28

The measures taken by the new government have been particularly noted by the newspapers. For example, the central agencies have been reduced from ten ministries to eight ministries, and the local areas have been reduced from sixteen provinces to seven provinces, and the towns have been reduced from 2,700 to 800, in order to save government expenses. The town and city councils are about to be dissolved, and the town chiefs and mayors will also serve as magistrates, all of whom will be appointed by the central government. According to reports, the future parliament will only have 100 members, of whom 75 will be appointed by the government, and the remaining 25 will be elected by professional groups. The old parliament had 274 members. (Havas dispatch, 20th)

Coup d'état Occurs Unexpectedly (London) 29

Reports of King Boris's assassination are completely unfounded. Military action began at two o'clock this morning. All public institutions have been occupied by military authorities, and crucial locations are heavily guarded by artillery and machine gun units. A notification was issued to shops and offices to cease work, so those going to work were turned back and pedestrian traffic was prohibited. Besides armed patrols, the streets were deserted. Prime Minister Muraviev was awakened early in the morning by his servant, who told him that the prime minister's residence was surrounded by troops. He urgently telephoned Minister of War Kissov, but a military officer answered, saying that private conversations were not allowed at this time. Muraviev said, "I am the Prime Minister." The officer replied, "You are not the Prime Minister." Then the phone line was cut. Other cabinet members who tried to make phone calls received the same response. Even the newly appointed cabinet members were quite surprised, as police officers went to their residences, urged them to get up, and took them to the police station. At first, everyone thought they had been arrested, but upon arriving at the police station, the police chief informed them that they had all been honorably appointed to the new government. After the troops occupied the capital, they simultaneously and strictly monitored incoming and outgoing communications. Even telephone calls from embassies required the approval of the authorities. When British Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen left the embassy, he was escorted by a military officer. A Reuters reporter only managed to get to the British Embassy at noon. As of now, hundreds of left-wing party members and communists have been arrested. (Reuters dispatch, 20th)

Bribery Case Exposes Official Corruption and Decay

Saito Cabinet in Japan Shaken; Kuroda Case Involves Many Important Figures; Prime Minister and Finance Minister's Responsibility Becomes a Problem; Military Factions and Political Parties Fight Secretly; Pro-Ugaki Faction Takes the Opportunity to Agitate 30

(Tokyo) The current cabinet's disciplinary problems have been fully exposed, causing great concern within the government. The cabinet's total resignation is certain, as a major incident involves not only Kuroda, the Vice Minister of Finance, but also Ohno Ryuta, the Chief of the Special Banks Section of the Banking Bureau, who was summoned by the prosecutor's office again this morning at seven o'clock. It is possible that this will affect important figures in the government, and the government's panic has reached an extreme level. Although they appear calm on the surface, they are secretly considering measures to deal with the aftermath. In particular, the responsibility of Finance Minister Takahashi for supervising his subordinates and Prime Minister Saito will become a problem. Before the regular cabinet meeting on the 22nd, the Prime Minister will summon the Finance Minister, the Interior Minister, and the Minister of Justice to hear about the situation and then discuss the government's course of action. Currently, the cabinet's total resignation is only a matter of time. However, considering that the Kuroda case is still under preliminary examination, they will temporarily observe the situation with caution, fully discuss measures to deal with the aftermath, and then carry out the total resignation. (Dentsu dispatch, 20th)

Cabinet Considers Advancing and Retreating 31

(Tokyo) With the formal indictment of Finance Vice Minister Kuroda Hideo yesterday, Finance Minister Takahashi feels the greatest responsibility. Political circles expect Takahashi to resign to take responsibility, but his resignation is bound to trigger a violent movement to overthrow the cabinet. Therefore, the resignation will have to take the form of a total resignation of all cabinet members. Finance Minister Takahashi is most concerned about this point. Although today is Sunday, the heads of the government are in frequent contact to find a good way to deal with the situation. (China United Press dispatch, 20th)

(Tokyo) The Kuroda Vice Minister issue has affected Ohno, the Chief of the Banking Section, and Aida, the administrator, and it is becoming increasingly urgent that it will reach Okubo, the Director of the Banking Bureau. The Ministry of Finance and the government are experiencing a major shock, and Finance Minister Takahashi's decision to advance or retreat is being given more attention, putting the political situation in crisis. (China United Press dispatch, 20th)

Hamaguchi's Son-in-Law Summoned 32

(Tokyo) The Tokyo District Court Prosecutor's Office had previously summoned Ohno, the Chief of the Special Banks Section of the Ministry of Finance. This morning at nine o'clock, they summoned Aida Iwao, the former Prime Minister Hamaguchi's son-in-law, who is the supervisor of the Taiwan Bank and the Korea Bank of the Ministry of Finance. At 9:10, they summoned Shito Motojiro, a supplementary bank inspector, investigated by Kuroda. The Director of the Banking Bureau, Okubo Teiji, himself feels in danger. Ohno, the Chief of the Special Banks Section, is the son-in-law of the former Minister of Justice, Hara Yoshimichi, and has a relationship with the 囗囗 problem under the order of Kuroda, the Vice Minister. Therefore, both Aida and Shito are suspected of taking bribes. (Dentsu dispatch, 20th)

Three More Arrested 33

(Tokyo) The bribery case of Finance Vice Minister Kuroda has suddenly expanded in scope. Although it was Sunday the 20th, all prosecutors of the prosecutor's office were present and summoned Ohno Ryuta, the Chief of the Special Banks Section of the Ministry of Finance under the jurisdiction of Vice Minister Kuroda, as well as Aida Iwao, a bank administrator, and Shito Motojiro, a former bank inspector. As a result of the serious questioning by the prosecutor's office, it was found that all three had committed dereliction of duty. They were prosecuted and imprisoned on the afternoon of the same day. (Japan United Press dispatch, 20th)

(Tokyo) Regarding the Kuroda Vice Minister issue, the Ministry of Justice, from Minister of Justice Koyama down, held a long meeting yesterday to discuss the future course of action. It is rumored that there are others who have been summoned, but they are not key figures and may not be as affected as some have reported, reaching Minister of Railways Mitsuchi and former Minister of Education Hatoyama. Successor to Vice Minister of Finance Decided 34

(Tokyo) Kuroda, the Vice Minister of Finance who was accused and imprisoned, has been dismissed. His successor has been internally decided to be Fujii Shinobu, the Director of the Budget Bureau of the Ministry of Finance. (Dentsu dispatch, 20th)

Military Factions and Political Parties Contend for Power 35

(Tokyo) Although the military is not entirely satisfied with the Saito Cabinet, they still consider it to have a compliant nature that listens to military orders. In this era of difficult childbirth for the next cabinet, they are still willing to support the current cabinet. However, since Elder Statesman Saionji came to Tokyo, he has been striving to restore constitutional government and suppress Hirayama, the Vice President of the Privy Council from the military faction, which has caused great indignation. Moreover, both the Seiyukai and Minseito parties recognize that it is not yet time to restore party politics and are planning to recommend General Ugaki, the Governor-General of Korea, as the next Prime Minister. Ugaki is determined to come to Tokyo on the 27th or 28th of this month to campaign. Ugaki is the most feared by the current military. Therefore, the military believes that if the Saito Cabinet carries out a total resignation, it will inevitably be taken advantage of by the political parties and the Ugaki faction, which is causing great concern. Therefore, they may plan to maintain the current cabinet. The corruption case of Finance Vice Minister Kuroda has actually stirred up disputes among various factions in the Japanese political and military circles, and its trend deserves the most attention. (China United Press dispatch, 20th)

Saionji Returns to Okitsu 36

(Tokyo) Elder Statesman Saionji came to Tokyo on the 3rd of this month and undertook the following tasks: (1) He met with Foreign Minister Hirota to instruct him on diplomatic steps, especially on diplomacy with China and the United States, urging him to recognize the international situation and not be manipulated by the military, so as not to lead Japan to national ruin. (2) He met with Minister of the Imperial Household Makino and Prime Minister Saito to have Ichiki Kitokuro, a supporter of constitutionalism, appointed as the President of the Privy Council, suppressing Vice President Hirayama. (3) In preparation for his death, he agreed that Privy Council President Ichiki and Minister of the Imperial Household Makino would act as Elder Statesman to assist the Emperor. With this work completed, this morning at one past ten, he and his secretary boarded a car and returned to his retirement villa in Okitsu. There were 500 police officers at Tokyo Station, with strict security to prevent assassination by various factions under the control of the military. (China United Press dispatch, 20th)

Bombing Case Near Vienna

Twelve Incidents in One Day; Retaliatory Acts by the Nazi Party; Military Police Deployed; Bombers All Escape 37

This morning, more than a dozen locations on the national railways and power lines throughout Austria were bombed simultaneously, and all of the perpetrators escaped without being caught. It is widely believed that these are retaliatory acts by the Nazi Party against the current government, and that they were carefully planned. Throughout the day, the Ministry of Public Security has made every effort to obtain the perpetrators with the assistance of the military police, but so far has achieved nothing. Among these twelve bombing incidents, three occurred in the suburbs of the capital. After several railway bridges were bombed, only broken rails remained suspended in the air. In Salzburg, two huge power poles were also blown up, plunging the entire city into darkness. There are six other bombing incidents that have been formally reported here, and there are several other cases of bombs being discovered but not detonated along railways in various places. The government has offered a reward to apprehend the main culprits in this case, and reports of bombings are still coming in. For example, this afternoon, three more locations on the tracks between Gamisch Partenkirchen and Innsbruck were bombed, resulting in very heavy losses. According to statistics, among the cases that have been reported today, all lines connecting the capital, except for the Franz Josef line, have been affected. (National Press dispatch, 19th)

Chicago

Major Fire at Stockyards; Twenty Dead and Injured; Material Losses Exceed Ten Million; Fire Started by Cigarette Butt Igniting Accumulated Fuel 38

Chicago: The Chicago Union Stockyards were careless today, and the fire spread extremely quickly. Within an hour, the entire area of one square mile was surrounded by flames. Before long, the fire spread to a hotel and two banks, and fanned by a strong wind, it threatened to move towards the northwest residential area. The people, seeing their houses in danger, were indescribably panicked. There were also several thousand spectators, and the police widely deployed sentry lines to prevent looting. Firefighters from within several miles rushed to help put out the fire. Seeing the dryness of the water, residents also organized water-carrying teams to fetch water from a distance to help. However, the fire continued to burn for several hours before it could be contained. The firefighters tried various methods to stop the spread of the fire. The fire was aided by the strength of the wind and was unstoppable. Therefore, they tried to place explosives at key points to reduce the fire's intensity. In this disaster, in addition to destroying several houses, several ammonia warehouses and oil pools were also destroyed. It is currently believed that twenty people were injured, including one police officer, and the losses exceed ten million dollars. It is truly a major disaster for Chicago. It is also said that the telephone operators at the stockyards did not leave their posts until the flames reached their switchboards and the telephone lines were burned. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Chicago: It is now believed that the cause of the fire is the same as the Great Chicago Fire of 1871, caused by someone unintentionally throwing an unextinguished cigarette butt into a bale of hay in a stable. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Chicago: It is estimated that the total loss from the fire reaches ten million dollars, including the destruction of fifteen large buildings, many residences, countless cattle and sheep sheds, warehouses, etc. Empty cars and freight-loaded vehicles were also affected. There is no definite report on the loss of livestock. A portion of the elevated railway line was also burned, leaving only a few steel pillars. The remaining houses are only great skeletons of steel, but still remain. Nearly three thousand people assisted the firefighters in fighting the blaze. All buildings within a radius of three kilometers were affected by the disaster. According to records, the slaughterhouse burned down employs a number of personnel equal to one-sixth of the entire population of Chicago, occupying an area of three square kilometers. The livestock sold and slaughtered there amounts to 15 million head per year. Now, the slaughtering machinery in the slaughterhouse has also been completely burned. According to an airmail pilot, he saw the flames soaring straight into the clouds, reaching a height of 1,200 meters, from the sky 120 kilometers away from Chicago. He thought that the entire city of Chicago was on fire. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Infant Health Competition in Nanjing; Finals Held; First Place Winner Called "Nanjing Child" 39

Opening of the Third Iron Exhibition 40

(Beiping) The opening ceremony of the Third Iron Exhibition was held today. He Yingqin, Yuan Liang, and others attended and gave speeches. Qian Zongze delivered a speech, hoping that all sectors would offer strict criticism. (Special dispatch, 20th)

(Beiping) The opening ceremony of the Third Iron Exhibition was held at the Taimiao at 3:00 PM on the 20th. Qian Zongze, Yu Yan, Zheng Baozhao, Zheng Daobao, Ge Guangting, He Yingqin, Yuan Liang, Wang Shuchang, Belgian Envoy Ji Youmu, and guests from all walks of life, totaling more than 300 people, attended. Qian Zongze, as chairman, reported on the significance of the Iron Exhibition, stating that the purpose of this event is to spread culture, support the development of national industry and commerce, enable society to understand the functions of railways, promote industry, regulate the economy, strive to promote production, increase national strength, and revive our Chinese nation. He hopes that the people of the whole country will guide and assist to achieve the effect of collective wisdom and effort. Next, Yu Yan reported on the preparations and the reform of railway administration. He Yingqin then gave a speech, stating that China was originally a country with backward production. In recent years, it has been plagued by Red bandits and the international situation is dangerous. Rural bankruptcies and industrial and commercial decline occur everywhere, and all construction cannot be carried out. Therefore, the central government has decided on a major plan to save the nation and survive, striving to suppress the Red bandits and promote production and construction. The opening of the Iron Exhibition at this time is of profound significance, as it can statistically analyze railway products across the country to provide opportunities for improvement. At the same time, material development, knowledge exchange, national assimilation, and military speed are all closely related to transportation. If transportation is inconvenient and transportation is hindered, the country and the people will suffer countless losses. While promoting production, we must strive for construction, hoping that everyone will follow the Premier's industrial plan, accelerate the completion of several main lines running through the country, and hope that future iron exhibitions will spread throughout the country, so that various productions will develop accordingly, and achieve the goal of prosperity and strength. Finally, Yuan Liang, Wang Shuchang, and others gave speeches one after another. The meeting adjourned at about 5 o'clock. After the ceremony, guests were invited to visit the exhibition hall. The Beining and Pinghan Pavilions were the most neatly arranged, except for the Specialty Pavilion. The Pinghan Pavilion also made a model train that actually ran in the hall, which was especially praised by the guests. The exhibition officially opened on the 20th. For the sake of popularization, no tickets will be charged for the first three days, and admission is free. (Central News Agency dispatch, 20th)

(Tianjin) Yu Yan, the Director of the Joint Transportation Department of the Ministry of Railways, who recently attended the Iron Exhibition in Beiping, has temporarily delayed his return due to unfinished business. (Special dispatch, 20th)

(Zhengzhou) Qian Zongze, the Vice Minister of Railways, recently went to Beiping to handle the funeral of his father. Now he is in Beiping participating in the National Railway Product Exhibition. (Central News Agency dispatch, 20th)

Ministry of Industry Plans to Independently Operate a Newspaper Manufacturing Factory 46

(Nanjing) According to the Ministry of Industry, the plan to establish a newspaper manufacturing factory was originally intended to be a joint official-commercial venture with major newspaper offices and bookstores in Shanghai. However, due to the January 28th Incident, the commercial parties had insufficient funds, so it was suspended. Since the demand for newspaper materials is very high in the country, after the nationalized ammonium sulfate factory was turned over to commercial operation, the 255,000 pounds of British Boxer Indemnity loan originally used to establish the ammonium sulfate factory, along with the 88,750 pounds of British Boxer Indemnity surplus due to the Ministry of Industry, totaling about 4.84 million national currency, will be used as the foundation for the newspaper factory. Four million yuan in public bonds will be issued, and the factory will be operated independently by the government. The Ministry's proposal and plan have been approved by the Administrative Yuan. The distribution of the factory's capital of 4.1 million yuan is planned as follows: 1.9 million for pulp and papermaking machinery, 1.9 million for hydroelectric power plants, and 300,000 for base buildings. The plan has now been sent to the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board for review. The board of directors is expected to approve it on the 28th of this month. This paper factory can produce about 35 tons of newspaper per day. (Special dispatch, 20th)

Britain Plans to Establish a Long-Distance Airline Between Singapore and Shanghai 47

According to those involved, British Imperial Airways recently planned to establish a route from Singapore to Shanghai, with Hong Kong as the center, connecting with the Shanghai-Guangdong line to form a long-distance airline between Shanghai, Hong Kong, and Singapore. In order to quickly realize this plan, Britain has recently sent personnel from Imperial Airways to China to contact the Chinese transportation authorities to prepare for the matter and discuss the period of flight between the two sides to facilitate cooperation. Once the negotiations between China and Britain are completed, preparations can begin and be realized in a short period of time. (Special dispatch, 20th)

Zhang Kailian Talks About the Rapid Progress of Hunan's Highways 61

(Nanjing) Zhang Kailian, the Director of Finance of Hunan Province, arrived in Nanjing. It is said that Hunan Province has always been financially poor. Although it has been reorganized over the years, it still cannot make ends meet. Therefore, the living expenses of public officials are still paid at a discount. However, construction projects have not been stopped due to lack of funds. At present, the progress of Hunan's highways is very rapid and can be called well-connected in all directions. The highway from Changsha to Nanchang will also be completed next month and will be open to traffic directly. There is also good news: After Mr. Tang invented the charcoal car, its structure was not as flexible as a gasoline car, so he further researched it. Now he has invented the use of alcohol instead of gasoline. After testing, the combustion power is no different from gasoline, and the price of alcohol needed per hour is cheaper than gasoline. The provincial government is currently planning to build a small-scale alcohol factory with a capital of 300,000 yuan. It is expected to be completed in the second half of the year. The raw materials for alcohol production are red potatoes and sorghum produced in Hunan Province. Once the alcohol factory is successful, all cars running on highways in Hunan Province will be converted to use alcohol, which can save a lot of money every year. (20th special telegram)

Ping Shen Through Train Problem 99

Yin Tong Talks About the Process of Negotiating the Through Train

Beiping Communication: Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau, published a speech after returning to Beiping, summarizing the process of the Yuguan Conference: After the Tanggu Armistice Agreement was signed on May 31 last year, the things we gradually resolved were the counties in the Luan Yu Ji Mi war zone and the reception of various ports of the Great Wall, the reorganization of the security team in the war zone, etc., which were all successfully concluded. The most difficult problem was the through train problem on the Tang Yu section of the Beining Railway. After extreme negotiations, the through train on the Tang Yu section was finally realized on August 13, and we were able to avoid direct relations with the puppet organization. At this time, the Japanese asked for a through train to Ping Shen. Due to various relations, we allowed them to talk about it again two months later. I took office as Director of the Beining Railway Bureau on October 27 last year. At that time, it was two months after the through train on the Tang Yu section. The documents requesting negotiations on the through train from the Japanese had been piled up on my desk. After I took office, I discussed this matter at the first bureau affairs meeting. At the same time, I had a meeting with specialized personnel in the bureau and drafted several plans, which I personally sent to the central government for reference. But the central government suddenly denied the through train negotiations in December last year, so we could not talk about it anymore. It is rumored that I discussed the through train matter in Yu this time. Without a clear order from the central government, why should I automatically do this? Moreover, my visit to Yu and meeting with various people was a chance encounter. (19th)

Xiamen Communication: Lin Jing, a notorious bandit in Xianyou, was previously incorporated into the 7th Regiment of the Security Team. He擅自移防仙遊 and had extorted money from the people. Song Xiqian, commander of the 36th Division and garrison commander of Quanzhou, disarmed Lin's troops in Putian on April 17, arrested 33 officers from Lin and below and sent them to Quanzhou. The people of Xianyou and Putian accused them of being victimized. The Party Department and Chamber of Commerce of Xianyou, Putian, and Jinjiang sent telegrams requesting that they be executed on the spot. Later, the provincial government ordered them to be sent to the province for interrogation. The people of Xingquan still insisted on execution on the spot. Song Xiqian returned to Quanzhou from Xiamen on the 7th and sent a telegram to the provincial government, saying that the people were angry and asked for permission to execute them on the spot. The special Party Department of the 36th Division also sent a telegram to the province requesting that it comply with public opinion. At the same time, various community organizations in Xingquan sent telegrams to the province, saying that Lin Jing had been harming Putian and Xianyou for ten years. Hearing that his gang was active in the province, they asked Commander Song to execute him on the spot to appease public anger and stop rumors. Therefore, the provincial government telegraphed the Quanzhou Garrison Command on the 12th, ordering Lin Jing and five of his gang to be executed by firing squad in Quanzhou. After receiving the telegram, Song Xiqian brought out Lin and his battalion commander Yang Da, company commander Yang Keng, Lin De, Lin Ying, and adjutant Fu Zixiong at 9:30 am on the 13th and tied them to Zhongshan Park for execution. When Lin was brought out, he still thought he was being sent to the province. When he saw the troops lined up and the executioner interrogated him, his face changed. He still pleaded with the executioner to convey his request to the division commander to give him a few more days, saying that someone outside was guaranteeing him. He pleaded several times and was finally pushed to the execution ground, where he died immediately after being hit by four bullets. The other five people also died together. Lin Chunmeng, the Xianyou Party Committee, was shot and killed by Lin this spring. His wife Huang Qingxia went to the execution ground to watch the execution. After the execution, the Quanzhou Garrison Command announced that "the case investigated that Lin Jing, Yang Da, Yang Keng, Lin De, Lin Ying, and adjutant Fu Zixiong (all from Xianyou), the commanders of the 7th Security Regiment, had been harming Putian and Xianyou for more than ten years, committing adultery, looting, arson, and murder, doing everything they could. The people cried and swallowed their voices. Last time, the provincial government approved the reorganization, originally hoping that they would repent and start anew. However, since the reorganization, the regiment commander and others have continued to do evil and abuse the good, adding to the harm. There must be several complaints or accusations from the people in all directions who come to the headquarters every day. In view of their crimes, it is impossible to record them all. In order to eliminate violence and maintain peace, the headquarters dispatched a team to disarm them and reported the situation to the Fujian Provincial Government for Chen and he. Now we have received a telegram authorizing execution on the spot to show vigilance, and we should comply. In addition to signing and sending the criminals to the execution ground for execution, we should announce it to the public." According to reports, Lin Jing is 34 years old this year and is from Dayun Village, Xianyou. He came from the green forest and was accepted as the commander of the 2nd Battalion of the Marine Corps. In 1919, he rebelled in Xianyou, and his firearms increased to more than 2,000 guns. Later, he was accepted as the 2nd Detachment of the Provincial Defense Army and transferred to Fuqing. Because of the harsh taxes, it caused a civil revolt. Thousands of people died in Fuqing, and 500 of Lin's troops also died. The provincial government ordered the suppression. In 1921, the Communist bandits captured Zhangzhou. Lin was reorganized by the navy as the 1st Detachment of the Suppression Red Army and stationed in Dongshan. Later, it was resolved by the 49th Division. Lin returned to Xianyou. During the 19th Route Army, Lin was accepted as the 4th Detachment of the People's Self-Defense Army, with more than 2,000 people. Later, it was reorganized as the 7th Security Regiment, with a thousand and three hundred guns in a response point. Then it was disarmed and arrested. Chen Guohui, a bandit in southern Fujian, belonged to Quanyong, and Lin belonged to Putian and Xianyou, both of whom were the only giants. (May 17)
