Expected Bumper Harvest for Suzhou and Wuxi Silkworms 102

Favorable Climate Leads to Excellent Development

Silkworm Seeds to be Under Unified Control This Autumn

Suzhou Dispatch: The two counties of Suzhou and Wuxi, situated near Taihu Lake, possess abundant mulberry fields and a renowned silk industry. Furthermore, with the early improvement of rearing methods and the excellent quality of cocoons, the silk industry has been steadily growing. However, it has been affected by the recent decline in silk prices and the bankruptcy of rural villages, leading to a gradual decrease in the number of silkworm farmers. Currently, the Department of Construction of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces has established the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Improvement Management Association to implement unified control, improve silkworm breeds, and compel farmers to purchase them in order to seek relief. This spring, the cold weather greatly affected silkworm farming, but fortunately, the county's silkworm rearing was delayed. The weather has now turned favorably warm, and the silkworms are developing well. Most of them have already passed their third molt and are developing excellently. In a week, they will be ready to spin cocoons. A bumper harvest of cocoons is expected this summer. Yesterday, our reporter investigated the situation from various sources, as follows:

The silkworm area in Wuxian County is roughly divided into four districts: (1) Guangfu, (2) Mudu, (3) the East and West Mountains of Dongting, and (4) Xiangshan. Among these, except for the Mudu district, which still adheres to traditional methods and does not know how to improve, the rest have purchased improved silkworm breeds and adopted new rearing methods. In the Guangfu district, the Wuxian County Agricultural Extension Office has established a guidance center to teach farmers how to raise silkworms, which has been going on for six or seven years and has achieved good results. This spring's silkworm farming is also going smoothly. However, in the Guangfu Shanzhen Bridge area, guided by the Suzhou Agricultural School, many of the early-hatched silkworms have died due to the weather's impact. The late-hatched ones are still in their first molt and should not experience any further mishaps. Few farmers in Dongting East Mountain raise silkworms, while West Mountain remains prosperous. The improved silkworm breeds in that area, especially the Pagoda and Tiger brands, account for the absolute majority. The rearing process is also good. Xiangshan is an industrial area, and silkworm farming is the main agricultural activity. In the autumn of the year before last, the Fengxi Silkworm Seed Manufacturing Plant invested in opening a guidance center to teach farmers to adopt new silkworm rearing methods. After three years of efforts and improvement, the number of silkworm farmers adopting new methods has increased from fifty or sixty households to more than a thousand. The annual cocoon yield has increased, and the quality has also improved. This spring's silkworm farming has been developing exceptionally well, with great prospects for a bumper harvest. The native silkworm breeds have mostly died and have gradually disappeared in recent years. Wuxi has always been the largest market for silkworm seeds. In previous years, the annual silkworm sales could reach 600,000 sheets of improved seeds. This spring, due to the increasing bankruptcy of farmers' economies and weak purchasing power, only 400,000 sheets were sold. The county's guidance center is hosted by the Shanxian County Agricultural Farm. This spring, the Huaxin Silk Factory has also invested in establishing a large-scale guidance center to teach silkworm farmers. Currently, the early-hatched silkworms have passed the 3rd molt, and the late-hatched ones are still in their first molt. They are developing well, and a good harvest is expected.

The Jiangsu Silkworm Seed Unified Control Regulation has been decided by the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Improvement Management Conference and will be implemented this autumn. Model areas and non-model areas will be designated. In the model areas, cocoon merchants will deduct twelve yuan per load when collecting cocoons to purchase silkworm seeds and force farmers to raise improved silkworm breeds. In non-model areas, public sales offices will be established to facilitate farmers' purchase. The association has now designated Wuxi County and the East and West Mountains of Dongting in Wuxian County as model areas and will soon establish silkworm seed public sales offices in Hushu Pass, Guangfu, Hengjing, and Xiangshan. (Shen Shi News Agency)

An Impressionistic Record of Economic Survey in Guangxi Province (Continued) 103

— Qian Jiaju

However, can this kind of rural lending really liberate farmers from the clutches of usury? Here, I record what Mr. Gao Yuanxun, who presides over the farmers' lending in this district, said to us: "The effect of this lending in rural areas is minimal. Farmers still seek help from usury and are still trapped under the high degree of exploitation by merchant capital. Because there are too many poor people here, a mere thirty or fifty thousand yuan is really a drop in the bucket and of no help. According to our estimates, the farmers' debt in this area amounts to 300,000 yuan. To help them, at least 500,000 yuan is needed to truly eliminate the exploitation of usurious capital. In fact, usury is not the main problem. The most frightening thing is the manipulation of agricultural product prices by merchants. For example, there is a collection and storage shop called Guangxinglong. When there is a spring famine, they lend peanut cakes or grain to farmers, agreeing to return sugar cane in the future. These peanut cakes are worth only two or three yuan, but they lend them out at the highest price of eight or nine yuan, with a monthly interest rate of three percent. When the farmers harvest the sugar cane, they are burdened with debt and have to take it to the sugar pressing shops, which are also opened by Guangxinglong. Thus, they can collect exorbitant fees. Of course, they can get some cheap sugar. After the sugar is pressed, the company that collects the sugar is also them. At this time, they can immediately suppress the sugar price very low. For example, the sugar in Liuzhou, when the price is high (between August and September), can be sold for thirteen or fourteen yuan per load. However, when the sugar is produced (October to December), it can only be sold for five or six yuan. Through this kind of exploitation, the rural areas are becoming poorer day by day, and the merchants or landlords are becoming richer. Now, 90 percent of those who borrow money from us are tenant farmers. These tenant farmers have all gone bankrupt from being self-sufficient farmers."

Mr. Gao's words deserve our deep attention because the exploitation of farmers by merchant capital is not unique to Liuzhou, but is the same throughout China. And the difficulty of achieving practical results due to the lack of funds for rural lending is not only the difficulty felt by the Reclamation and Water Conservancy Pilot Area, but also the difficulty felt by all of China's so-called farmers' banks, credit lending cooperatives. The total population of the pilot area is only 40,000, and the debt amount has reached more than 300,000 yuan. Then, the debt amount of Guangxi's 12 million people should be at least 100 million yuan. Can such a serious rural financial problem be solved by relying solely on credit lending? Perhaps this is worth our reflection.

In addition to agricultural and forestry institutions, Liuzhou is also a pilot area for Guangxi's provincial-run factories. The three new industries in Guizhou Province in recent years—sulfuric acid plant, alcohol plant, and mechanical plant—except for the sulfuric acid plant located in Wuzhou, the rest are located in Jila (about ten miles from the city) in Liuzhou. Sulfuric acid and alcohol are both basic chemical industries in modern times, and the importance of mechanical plants is even more well known. Therefore, on our last day in Liuzhou, we went to visit them.

The planning of the alcohol plant originally started in the 16th year of the Republic of China. At that time, the authorities of Guizhou Province were determined to open up highways and were therefore concerned about the consumption of automobile fuel. They thought that alcohol could be used as a substitute for gasoline, so they prepared for the Guangxi Alcohol Plant. Later, due to financial constraints, progress was slow. After the military uprising in the 18th year, the political situation was chaotic, and everything was completely stalled. It was not until the 20th year of the Republic of China, after the cooperation between Guangdong and Guangxi, that they continued to start. In June of the 21st year, it officially started production. The factory works eight hours a day, producing about 800 catties of alcohol. After three days, it is distilled once, yielding 1,400 catties of 98-degree alcohol. The raw material for alcohol is temporarily using tangerine water, which is the distilled water after sugarcane is pressed for sugar. These are all local products of Liuzhou. Now, merchants from all over know that the alcohol plant needs tangerine water and have inventory. They bring the goods to the factory to test the quality and then negotiate the price, pay a deposit, and transport it back to the factory for storage on schedule. However, because the supply of tangerine water is limited and the cost is too expensive, it now costs seven dimes per catty of alcohol to make. Adding the consolidated tax, transportation costs, etc., it costs about four dimes to transport to Guangzhou, and the selling price in Guangzhou is only this amount. It is said that they also know that the cost of using tangerine water is expensive, but because the authorities were concerned at the beginning not about the cost, but about whether the machine is suitable or not, whether the product is good after starting, and whether there is a market. So they temporarily used tangerine water to test. Their original plan was to use miscellaneous grains, so the factory site was not set in Wuzhou, where transportation is convenient and the land is in the center, but in Liuzhou, where the land is vast and the miscellaneous grains are abundant. They are now planning to make alcohol from miscellaneous grains. The residue left over from making alcohol from miscellaneous grains is used to feed livestock, and the livestock is sold to exchange for miscellaneous grains. The two expenditures are just offset, so the cost of raw materials can be completely saved. Now, 90 percent of the products of the Liuzhou Alcohol Plant are sold to Guangzhou. We firmly believe that if the alcohol industry can develop, it will not only be enough to resist a part of Guizhou Province's leak, but also one of the most promising national industries in our country. However, after visiting the Liuzhou Alcohol Plant, there is something that we think is not perfect, that is, after the factory was changed to the Industry and Commerce Bureau (formerly under the Construction Department, after March of the 10th year, it belonged to the Industry and Commerce Bureau), Director Yang Zhuo also merged their accounting into the Industry and Commerce Bureau, so that not only the cost of alcohol, how the sales are, and what the selling price is, the people in the factory are completely inexplicable. Even when we asked whether the factory has been making money or losing money recently and how the profits and losses are, from the factory director to the accounting director, they all stared blankly and didn't know how to answer. On the one hand, this is a manifestation of Mr. Yang's responsible spirit, but a factory without independent accounting is something we ultimately think is not good.

County Magistrate Ma immediately summoned Wang Yongnian and Wang Yingkuan, who were in custody, for interrogation. The injured policeman Dai Chengfa also came to court to confront them and confirm the facts. According to Wang Yingkuan's confession, Wang owed 20 yuan for membership fees and took the cow as collateral, which was not robbery. The assault on the police and seizure of weapons was due to a misunderstanding at night that the police team was a bandit and did not dare to resist arrest. The seized guns and cannons had been handed over to the village head Li Deyi, but their whereabouts were unknown. It was ordered that Wang Yingkuan be shackled and sent to prison, and Wang Yongnian be sent to the police detective team for custody, pending investigation.

Gaoyou Recent News on the Yangqing Highway Project 110

Since the construction of new bridges along the Grand Canal on the Yangqing Highway in Jiangsu Province, it has now been completed. However, there are still high and low spots on the road surface along the levee. The engineering office of the Jiangsu Construction Department has sent personnel to repair and level the sections to facilitate transportation. The entire road project is expected to be completed at the beginning of next month, and it will be open to traffic in the middle of next month.

Ge Zuoqin Commits Suicide to Prove Innocence 111

Ge Zuoqin, the son of Ge Zhiqian, a resident of Hangjia Township in the 11th District of this county, is 18 years old and works as a teacher. Recently, a busybody spread rumors that Zuoqin had an affair with a widow surnamed Chen. His father heard about it and believed it to be true, so he severely reprimanded him. Zuoqin, feeling wronged and unable to clear his name, had a moment of despair and committed suicide with a razor the night before, cutting his throat. Blood flowed like a river. When his family discovered it, it was impossible to save him. It was a tragic end.

Special Issue on the National Financial Conference

The Origin and Preparatory Situation of Convening the National Financial Conference The Ministry previously received 112

an order from the Executive Yuan in the 149th Executive Yuan meeting to reduce the additional tax on cultivated land and abolish miscellaneous taxes and levies. The implementation measures were telegraphed to the provincial and municipal governments for compliance, and it was ordered to be noted, along with copies of the implementation measures. It was found that item three of the original document stipulated that the Ministry of Finance should convene representatives from the provincial and municipal financial authorities and economic circles in Beijing in June of this year for a meeting. The Ministry of Finance should comply with this. Preparatory committee members were appointed on March 26 to engage in preparations. However, the issues to be discussed at the meeting, such as reducing the additional tax on cultivated land and abolishing miscellaneous taxes and levies, are all related to local budgets. The start of the 23rd year is approaching, so the date of the meeting was slightly advanced to May 21 of this year. It has been submitted to the Executive Yuan meeting and approved for advance. Immediately, five types of conference regulations were formulated. Based on these regulations, relevant ministries, committees, and offices, as well as provincial and municipal governments, were consulted to recommend representatives, and the directors of the provincial and municipal finance departments and the directors of the municipal finance bureaus were asked to attend the meeting in Beijing. The proposals, reports, and plans should be sent to the Ministry ten days before the conference for collation. Experts were also selected and hired to attend the meeting for joint discussion. The internal and external personnel of the Ministry of Finance who should attend the meeting were also designated separately. Subsequently, on April 11, Qin Fen, the Permanent Vice Minister of the Ministry, was appointed as the Secretary-General of the conference, and personnel were selected to organize the Secretariat to start work. The published regulations, the members of the conference preparatory committee, and the titles of the important officials of the Secretariat are listed below.

A Regulations I Regulations of the National Financial Conference 113

Announced by the Ministry on April 20, 23rd Year Article 1 The Ministry of Finance convenes the National Financial Conference to organize the national cultivated land tax, improve the tax system, abolish miscellaneous taxes and levies, and compile local budgets. Article 2 This conference is organized by the following members: 1. Representatives of the Executive Yuan, representatives of the National Economic Committee, representatives of the Executive Yuan's Political Affairs Committee in Peiping, representatives of the Directorate General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics, and representatives of relevant ministries and committees under the Executive Yuan; 2. Representatives of provincial and municipal governments (cities directly under the Executive Yuan); 3. The Minister, Vice Minister, Chief Secretary, Counselors, and heads of each department of the Ministry of Finance; 4. Directors of provincial finance departments or their representatives; 5. Directors of municipal finance bureaus;

6. Heads of directly affiliated financial institutions designated by the Ministry of Finance;

7. Experts selected and hired by the Ministry of Finance.

Article 3 The director of the provincial finance department should not send a representative unless it is absolutely necessary.

Article 4 The Minister of Finance is the Chairman of the conference, and the Vice Minister is the Vice Chairman.

Article 5 The conference venue is located in the Ministry of Finance in the capital. Article 6 The conference period is set from May 21 to 27, 23rd year of the Republic of China. If necessary, the Minister of Finance may extend or shorten the period.

Article 7 The scope of discussion of the conference is limited to the cases submitted by the Ministry of Finance and the motions proposed by the members stipulated in Article 2.

Article 8 A quorum for the opening of the conference is the attendance of more than half of the registered members.

Article 9 The resolution of motions at the conference depends on the majority of the attending members. In the event of an equal number of votes for and against, the Chairman shall make the final decision.

Article 10 If any member has a proposal, it must be submitted to the Secretariat of the Conference three days before the opening of the conference for prior arrangement and inclusion in the agenda. If there is a temporary proposal, it must be submitted in writing to the Chairman with the joint signature of five or more members for consideration and inclusion in the agenda.

Article 11 If various motions need to be reviewed, the Chairman shall designate personnel from among the members to form a review committee to review them. For motions that need to be reviewed under special circumstances, the Chairman shall temporarily designate a special review committee to review them.

Article 12 The resolutions of the conference shall be selected and implemented separately by the Ministry of Finance.

Article 13 The conference shall establish a secretariat with a number of staff to be in charge of various affairs. Its regulations will be determined separately. Article 14 The travel expenses of the members of the conference, except for the experts selected and hired by the Ministry of Finance, shall be borne by the respective organizations that select and send them to attend, and shall be allowed as regular expenses.

Article 15 If there are any matters not covered in these regulations, the Ministry of Finance may amend them at any time.

II Measures for Proposals to the National Financial Conference 114

Published by Ministry Order on April 21, 23rd Year (1) When drafting a proposal, sufficient reasons and specific measures must be listed separately for the convenience of discussion.

(2) Matters that are specific to one locality and do not have a general nature should not be listed as proposals.

(3) All proposals must be sent to the Secretariat of the National Financial Conference of the Ministry of Finance three days before the opening of the conference for collation and printing.

(4) The order of submission of each proposal is as follows:

1. Those submitted by the Minister or Vice Minister of Finance

2. Those proposed by members

(5) When members submit proposals, they should be submitted in groups according to the following regulations:

First Group

Second Group

Third Group

Fourth Group

(6) Each proposal must be written separately on a separate sheet of paper according to the following format: 1. Group (mark the group number according to the previous article)

2. Proposer (attendance qualification and name)

3. Topic

4. Reason

5. Measures

(7) Each proposal must be a separate piece of writing. Do not connect two proposals on one sheet of paper.

(8) For any temporary proposal, the proposal should still be written in accordance with the format and submitted directly to the Chairman or Secretary-General before or during the meeting for consideration and inclusion in the agenda for discussion. Article 13 If a member has a major issue, he may make a temporary motion, but it must be seconded by three or more attending members.

Chapter 4 Review Committee

Article 14 Any proposal that cannot be resolved immediately at the general meeting may be submitted to the review committee for review, but the chairman may also decide to submit it for review first if he deems it necessary.

Article 15 The review committee is divided into the following groups: (1) The first group is responsible for matters related to cultivated land tax and additional taxes in various provinces.

(2) The second group is responsible for matters related to the reorganization of old taxes, the abolition of miscellaneous taxes and levies, and the improvement of local tax systems.

(3) The third group is responsible for determining the deadlines for the establishment of local budgets at all levels and stipulating the procedures for compilation, submission, and review.

(4) The fourth group is responsible for proposal matters that do not belong to the above groups.

Article 16 The members of the review committee of each group shall be designated by the chairman from among the members.

Article 17 Each group of the review committee shall have a chairman and four standing committee members, who shall be designated by the chairman from among the members of the group.

Article 18 The meeting time of the review committee shall be determined and notified by the chairman of each group.

Article 19 The review committee shall report the review results of each case to the general meeting, and the chairman shall attend to explain. If he deems it necessary to amend it, he shall propose an amendment to the general meeting.

Chapter 5 Voting

Article 20 The resolution of motions at this meeting depends on the majority of the attending members. In the event of an equal number of votes for and against, the chairman shall make the final decision.

Honorable Chairman Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Finance 115

III Rules of Procedure for the National Financial Conference 116

Published by Ministry Order on April 21, 23rd Year Chapter 1 General Provisions

Article 1 The seats of members shall be determined by drawing lots.

Article 2 The Minister of Finance shall be the Chairman of the Conference, and the Vice Minister shall be the Vice Chairman. If the Chairman is absent due to business, the Vice Chairman shall act as the Chairman.

Article 3 The meeting time shall be decided by the Chairman and included in the agenda for prior notification.

Article 4 The motions and agenda shall be printed and distributed to each member in advance.

Chapter 2 Meetings

Article 5 This conference must have a quorum of more than half of the registered members present before it can be opened.

Article 6 All speakers must first stand up and report their number.

Article 7 No more than two members may speak at the same time during the meeting. If two or more members report numbers at the same time, the Chairman shall designate the order in which they speak.

Article 8 Members may not discuss matters outside the scope of the motion during the discussion.

Article 9 The time for each member to speak shall not exceed five minutes.

Article 10 No member may speak more than twice on the same motion, but this restriction does not apply to questioning, answering, or calling attention to.

Article 11 The Chairman may declare the end of the discussion during the meeting. Article 12 If it is found during the meeting that the motion is inconsistent or conflicts with the current laws and regulations of the National Government, the proposer may apply for modification or withdrawal.

Chapter 3 Temporary Motions

Article 21 When voting, the chairman shall first put the motion to be voted on to a vote. After the vote, no further discussion of the motion shall be allowed.

Chapter 6 Attendance and Absence

Article 22 If a member is unable to attend due to illness or other reasons, he must state the reasons to the Chairman for leave of absence.

Article 23 Members shall sign their names on the attendance book upon attendance.

Article 24 Members may not leave the meeting after attending unless the meeting is adjourned or on break, or with the permission of the Chairman.

Chapter 7 Supplementary Provisions

Article 25 Matters not covered in these rules shall be amended by resolution of the conference.

Secretariat of the National Financial Conference Outline 117

Promulgated by order of the Ministry on April 20, Year 23

Article 1: This Secretariat, under the direction of the Minister of Finance, shall handle matters pertaining to the National Financial Conference.

Article 2: This Secretariat shall have one Secretary-General who shall preside over all affairs of the Secretariat. He shall be appointed by the Minister of Finance.

Article 3: This Secretariat shall organize motions into the following groups:

Group 1: Responsible for organizing motions related to land tax and surcharges from various provinces.

Group 2: Responsible for organizing motions related to abolishing old taxes and miscellaneous levies, and improving local tax systems.

Group 3: Responsible for organizing motions related to setting deadlines for the establishment of local budgets at all levels, and stipulating procedures for compilation, submission, and review.

Group 4: Responsible for motions not belonging to the above groups.

Vice Chairman, Vice Minister of Finance, Zou Lin 118

Article 4: Each of the above groups shall have one Chief Secretary and a number of Secretaries.

Article 5: This Secretariat shall establish the following departments to handle affairs:

1. Document Department: Responsible for drafting, receiving, dispatching, translating telegrams, proofreading, and safeguarding official seals.

2. Agenda Department: Responsible for compiling and printing the agenda, shorthand reporting, organizing meeting minutes, and editing the daily bulletin of the conference.

3. General Affairs Department: Responsible for accounting, general affairs, printing, etc.

4. Public Relations Department: Responsible for receiving members and guests, liaising with journalists, and distributing the daily bulletin of the conference.

Each of the above departments shall have one Chief Officer, a number of Officers, and a number of Clerks.

Article 7: Each department of this Secretariat may, due to operational necessity, be divided into sections for handling affairs. The names of the sections shall be determined by each department.

Article 8: The personnel of each group and department of this Secretariat shall be appointed by the Secretary-General from the existing staff of the Ministry of Finance upon submission of a request. However, in special circumstances, the Secretary-General may select suitable personnel separately and submit a request for appointment.

Article 9: Laborers needed by this Secretariat shall be seconded from the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance.

Article 10: The office of this Secretariat shall be located in the Ministry of Finance.

Article 11: This Secretariat shall be dissolved upon completion of all matters after the close of the National Financial Conference and reported to the Minister of Finance.

Article 12: Detailed rules for handling affairs of this Secretariat shall be determined separately.

Article 13: This Outline shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Detailed Rules for Handling Affairs of the Secretariat of the National Financial Conference 119

Promulgated by order of the Ministry on April 21, Year 23

Article 1: These Detailed Rules are formulated in accordance with Article 12 of the Outline of this Secretariat.

Article 2: This Secretariat shall handle all affairs in accordance with these Detailed Rules.

Article 3: The duties of the staff of this Secretariat are as follows:

(1) The Secretary-General shall be in charge of all affairs of the Secretariat.

(2) The Chief Secretaries and Secretaries shall be responsible for organizing the conference and the motions of each group.

(3) The Chief Officers, Officers, and Clerks shall be responsible for the affairs of each department.

Article 4: The Document Department shall maintain the following registers:

(1) Circular Register

(2) Submission Register

(3) Incoming and Outgoing Document Register

(4) Dispatch Register

(5) Filing Register

Article 5: The Agenda Department shall maintain the following registers:

(1) Agenda Register

(2) Shorthand Record Register (divided into two types: Conference and Review Committee)

(3) Meeting Minutes Register (divided into two types: General Assembly and Review Committee)

(4) Register of Documents for Publication

Article 6: The General Affairs Department shall maintain the following registers:

(1) Budget and Final Account Statement

(2) Daily Income and Expenditure Ledger

(3) Register of Incoming and Outgoing Goods

(4) Register of Incoming and Outgoing Printed Documents (divided into three types: Gazette, Daily Bulletin, and Other Documents)

Article 7: The Public Relations Department shall maintain the following registers:

(1) Member Registration Register

(2) Member Attendance Register

(3) Member Leave Register

Vice Chairman, Vice Minister of Finance, Qin Fen 120

(4) Guest Name List

(5) Journalist Interview Record

(6) Document Publication Register

(7) Daily Bulletin Printing Register

Article 8: Documents and telegrams received by this Conference shall be summarized and recorded by the Document Department and submitted to the Secretary-General for review. Important documents shall be submitted to the Chairman for review.

Article 9: Documents and telegrams sent out by this Conference shall be drafted by the Document Department and submitted to the Secretary-General for approval. After being copied, translated, and proofread, they shall be summarized and recorded before dispatch. Important documents shall be submitted to the Chairman for approval.

Article 10: Proposed motions and reviewed cases shall be organized, numbered, printed, and compiled by the Agenda Department after submission for review. They shall then be compiled into the agenda and distributed to all members.

Article 11: All resolutions and minutes shall be organized and compiled into a report by the Agenda Department in sequence. After the close of the conference, they shall be compiled and transferred to the Document Department for filing and publication.

Article 12: When the General Assembly or group meetings are held, the secretaries of each group shall be present to record the proceedings, and the staff of each department shall be present to liaise and take care of all matters.

Article 13: All expenses related to the conference shall be budgeted by the General Affairs Department and submitted to the Chairman for approval through the Secretary-General. After the conference is concluded, a final account statement shall be prepared and submitted for verification.

Article 14: All completed cases shall be submitted to the Document Department for classification and filing.

Article 15: Matters not covered in these Detailed Rules shall be handled by the Secretary-General at his discretion or submitted to the Chairman for instructions.

Article 16: These Detailed Rules shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Member Reception Measures 122

1. Members arriving in Nanjing must first report to the Public Relations Department of this Conference Secretariat (located inside the Ministry of Finance in Citang Lane, turning north after entering the main gate), draw their seat number, and collect their attendance badge.

2. Members entering and leaving should use the main gate of the Ministry of Finance in Citang Lane for ease of reception.

3. Members attending the General Assembly and Review Committee meetings should sign in at the designated location in the Public Relations Department, and staff will guide them to their seats.

4. If members need to contact the relevant departments of the Ministry of Finance regarding conference matters, the Public Relations Department will provide guidance.

5. If members are unfamiliar with the situation in Nanjing, they may inquire and contact the Public Relations Department at any time (8:00 AM to 8:00 PM daily).

6. Any news releases related to the conference from members must be submitted to the Public Relations Department for unified release to avoid discrepancies.

Measures for Receiving Journalists 123

1. Journalists wishing to cover news at this conference must be introduced in writing by the person in charge of the newspaper or news agency they serve, and after approval by the conference, they may receive a journalist entry pass. However, each newspaper or news agency is limited to one person.

2. The Public Relations Department of this Conference Secretariat will liaise with journalists covering news.

3. News releases of this conference will be submitted by each group and department to the Public Relations Department for submission to the Secretary-General for review before unified distribution.

4. Journalists shall not publish records that have not been approved by this Conference Secretariat.

Ministry of Railways Orders Two Railway Bureaus to Report on the Situation of Various Levies and Miscellaneous Taxes in Order to Propose Abolition at the Financial Conference 125

The Ministry of Railways yesterday issued instructions to the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, stating that the National Financial Conference convened by the Ministry of Finance is about to open, and the Ministry of Railways will also send personnel to attend. This is an opportune time to propose the abolition of existing improper and excessive levies and miscellaneous taxes on railways nationwide in order to reduce the burden on merchants and civilians. All freight on each railway, in addition to freight charges, all other taxes of any nature, should be urgently reported by telegraph, including the name of the tax and the general tax rate, and then continue to submit detailed reports. It is essential to handle this matter conscientiously. After receiving this order, the railway bureaus immediately ordered their subordinates to investigate and report.

French Concession

Rent Dispute in Xicheng Lane: Mediation with Representatives of Both Sides Convened Yesterday, Expected to be Resolved Satisfactorily Soon 127

Xicheng Lane on Ximen Road and Malan Road in the French Concession has more than 140 houses. Since the landlord Sun Chuanfang took back the houses and managed them himself, he organized the Yiyuan Company to inform all tenants that they must uniformly renew their contracts and are not allowed to be in arrears with their rent. Staff are sent daily to collect and extort payments. The content of the contract is entirely one-sided, and other examples are particularly harsh. It stipulates that the rent must be paid in full by the fifth of each month, otherwise they will be ordered to vacate the house. The intention is nothing more than to make the old tenants unable to live, so that new tenants can be replaced, and huge small rents can be collected, or it is beautifully called deposit rent. In addition to three months, an additional 3 yuan per room will be charged for tap water. Subletting by three tenants is also restricted, which has aroused the resentment of all tenants and caused disputes that have lasted for many days. The current tenants, in addition to hiring lawyer Wu Kaisheng to protect their rights and interests in accordance with the law, have submitted the landlord's illegal and coercive contract to the Shanghai Committee for Reviewing Rent Disputes, requesting verification. The committee convened representatives of both sides to a meeting at the Fenglinqiao Association at 3:00 PM yesterday to mediate the dispute. Tenants' representatives Yao Xingyuan, Gu Mingjia, Weng Jixiang, Zhang Xingren, and Jiang Zhenfang, as well as landlord's representative lawyer Wu Zhenming, attended on time. Chen Lengseng, director of the Committee for Reviewing Rent Disputes, interviewed the representatives of both sides separately and then ordered the representatives of both sides to talk on the spot. The focus of the dispute was on the articles of the contract. In addition, regarding the harassment by rent collectors, Mr. Chen advised both parties that since the tenants had hired lawyer Wu to handle the matter, each tenant should raise opinions or make improvements to any unfavorable conditions in the contract and submit them to lawyer Wu together. Lawyer Wu would then schedule a negotiation with landlord's representative lawyer Wu to resolve the matter. The tenants could also request the landlord to replace the harassing rent collectors. At that time, there were no objections to this method, so it was decided to proceed in accordance with this principle to resolve the matter as soon as possible, and the results would be reported to the Review Committee for cancellation. The parties deliberated until around 4:00 PM before dispersing.

A dispute that has been going on for a long time is expected to be resolved soon.

The New Persian Consulate will be Officially Established on a Scheduled Date 128

New Voice News Agency reports that the first Persian Consul-General in Shanghai, Mr. Austrufan, has been ordered to come to Shanghai and has now rented a consulate building. The location is conveniently located between the Xieqiao General Association and the Italian Consulate-General. The consulate will move in and begin operations on June 15. When the consulate is established in the future, a number of officials will be dispatched to Shanghai from Persia. The number will depend on the needs after establishment. The number of Persian overseas Chinese in China is not large, about 100 people, including a small number of overseas Chinese residing in the northeast. There are also very few Chinese traveling to Persia. He hopes that the relationship between China and Persia will become closer in the future, and that commerce will gradually develop. Persia is currently moving forward on the road of development, and China is also becoming stronger and more prosperous. In addition, the reporter learned that the first certificate from the King of Persia to the Chinese government was sent to Shanghai yesterday (19th). Mr. Austrufan plans to personally take someone to Nanjing to submit the certificate to the Minister of Foreign Affairs after the establishment of the consulate.

The Eight Provinces Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau

The Entire Business is Determined to be Government-Run; The Central Government Approved 1 Million as Capital; All Commercial Shares Paid by Various Provinces will be Returned 136

Dagong News Agency reports that since November 27 last year, representatives from eight provinces established a preparatory office in Shanghai to determine commercial shares of 1 million. The provincial and municipal governments and rice merchants raised funds for the remaining 1 million of working capital, which was allocated by the central government. The business was of a government-supervised and merchant-operated nature, and Gu Xinyi and Wu Huanru were elected as the director and deputy director to carry out the preparatory work. The deadline for payment of shares was January 10 this year. When more than half of the commercial shares were paid, a shareholders' meeting was held to officially establish the bureau.

Difficulty in Raising Funds 137

Up to the beginning of last month, only Jiangxi, Hubei, Anhui and Shanghai provinces and cities had paid their shares, totaling 350,000 yuan. Other provinces repeatedly urged but failed to remit. As a result, the Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau became virtually stagnant. Bureau Director Gu Xinyi went to Jiangxi last month due to difficulties in raising funds, and met with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to request instructions. It has been decided that:

Government-Run 138

The central government previously approved 1 million of working capital as operating capital. The transportation and sales head office will be located in Shanghai and chaired by Gu Xinyi, appointed by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. Branch offices or transportation and sales agencies will be established in various commercial port areas in the country, and will be determined at any time depending on the business situation. Now, after the Jiangxi Camp orders arrive in Shanghai, they will start to proceed. Dagong News Agency reporters went directly to Mr. Gu yesterday to inquire about the matter. It is said that Chairman Chiang Kai-shek is very concerned about relieving the rural areas, so he attaches great importance to the Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau. Unfortunately, after half a year, the shares of the provinces are still less than half, which is very regrettable. Now that it has been decided to be government-run, the provinces have already paid

The Commercial Shares will be Returned 139

It is purely operated by the government, but 200,000 yuan of the 350,000 yuan of commercial shares were raised by the provincial and municipal governments and included under the commercial share item. Whether this share will be fully refunded in the future or allocated as an official operating capital item still needs to be requested for instructions before it can be handled. The name and authority of the government agency to which the Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau is affiliated must be determined by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. After the above two issues are resolved, it can be officially established.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables to Order the Release of Soybean Cakes Detained in Guangdong Province. The Place of Origin Should be Distinguished and No Blanket Detention Should be Allowed 140

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously received cables from the Guangdong Provincial Northern and Southern Ports Association and the Miscellaneous Grain Association, stating that the Guangdong Provincial donation tax contractors, without distinguishing the origin of soybean cakes, forcibly stated that the products of factories in Shanghai and Hankou were imported from the Eastern Provinces, resulting in the detention of more than 20 boats of bean cakes, amounting to more than 18,200 pieces. The Chamber asked for assistance, and the Chamber cabled to the Guangdong Provincial Government for release. This was recorded in the previous report. It is now learned that the Chamber has received a letter from the local Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Association, stating that the Guangdong contractors are forcibly detaining soybean cakes from the Shanghai Xixi Factory. The Chamber has cabled the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Guangdong Provincial Government, asking them to order the release immediately to protect the domestic soybean cake production. The original cable is recorded below.

Cable to the Executive Yuan 141

To the esteemed Executive Yuan, Ministry of Finance, Nanjing:

On the 19th of this month, we received a letter from the Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Association, stating that: “Our factory’s soybean cakes were detained in Guangdong and designated as imported from the Eastern Provinces, and heavy taxes were forcibly collected. We implore a cable order for immediate release, pending instructions with utmost urgency.”

Upon investigation, soybean cakes, peanut cakes, and other similar products are manufactured by factories located in Suzhou, Shanghai, and Hankou, all with distinguishable county jurisdictions and verifiable factory locations. Furthermore, the soybeans needed as raw materials are a common agricultural product in various provinces and are not exclusive to the three Eastern Provinces. The five provinces of Shandong, Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangsu, located near the production areas, still have a surplus of local materials. Since the customs blockade of the three Eastern Provinces, the taxation of soybeans transported to Shanghai has been heavy. For the sake of profit, merchants would never abandon the nearby and cheap sources in favor of distant and expensive ones. The Guangdong contractors are ignorant of the commercial situation and unwilling to investigate the matter honestly. They only know to rely on their arbitrary and fabricated claims, intending to maximize profits by illegal means. This is an egregious act of destroying the real economy.

Therefore, we hereby cable to the esteemed Ministry and Department to request a review and order the Guangdong Provincial Government to strictly instruct the Chenfeng Company to faithfully comply with the original plan, distinguish the place of origin, and clarify the boundaries of taxable and tax-exempt products. No blanket detention should be allowed to cause disturbances and accumulation.

Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully submits.

Letter to the Guangdong Provincial Government 142

Factories that can manufacture soybean cakes are all located in Wuxi, Kunshan, and Wujin counties in Jiangsu Province, and within the jurisdiction of Shanghai. The soybeans used are sourced from the five provinces of Shandong, Henan, Anhui, Hubei, and Jiangsu, near the production areas. There are verifiable factories and verifiable facts. Therefore, we hereby attach a photo form and submit this letter for review and forwarding to the contractors, to check each one and quickly release the wrongly detained goods. If you think there is something that must be taken seriously, in the future, for soybean cakes shipped from Shanghai to Guangdong, our association can notify the Miscellaneous Grain Association to issue a certificate, certifying the name of the factory and the place of origin of the raw materials, which will be carried with each shipment to Guangdong for identification. We hope you will check and implement this.

Problems Worth Noting in the Sino-Japanese Consolidation of Old Debts; Total Debt Amounted to More Than 590 Million 143

New Voice News Agency reports that, according to reliable sources, the issue of Sino-Japanese consolidation of old debts is still under discussion and has not been formally proposed. From the perspective of our country, if the Japanese side really has this proposal, the authorities have no reason to refuse. However, there is a more difficult point worth noting or studying by the Chinese people, that is, Japan also has a considerable number of old debts regarding the construction of railways in Northeast China. For example, the 2.47 million loan for the Xin-Feng-Ji-Chang Railway in April 1908, the 5 million loan for the Si-Zheng Railway in December 1915, the 6.5 million loan for the Ji-Chang Railway in May 1917, the 2.6 million short-term loan for the Si-Zheng Railway in December 1918, and the 22.5 million loan for the Si-Tao Railway in 1919 and 1920 are considered by the Japanese side to have no relationship with our country, and are instead being negotiated with the puppet created by Japan (last year Japan had already made this informal statement). Therefore, when consolidating Sino-Japanese old debts, this point really involves the issue of recognizing the puppet organization. However, some people think that it will not be so difficult. In order to avoid de facto recognition of the puppet organization, our country still recognizes that there is this debt for old debts in the Northeast, but it must be stated that under the Japanese force of grabbing and occupying, the Chinese government cannot fulfill the obligations of the loan contract until the Northeast is recovered, and it is stated that the right to claim damages is reserved. According to a reporter’s investigation, the total number of Sino-Japanese debts is more than 590.47 million Japanese yen. In addition, there is the Nishihara loan of 110 million yuan, which our country has never recognized.

Yangtze River Shanghai Port Dredging Project Resets Boat-Striking Buoys 144

Regarding the Yangtze River Estuary Shanghai port dredging project and the reinstallation of boat-striking buoys, the Hydrographic Office issued a navigation notice yesterday stating that the location is in sections 7, 8, and 9 of the Shanghai port, i.e., approximately 121 degrees 30 minutes east longitude and approximately 31 degrees 15 minutes north latitude. Within the above sections, the dredging project has a deadline for completion, and all dredgers will be removed at the same time. Buoys numbered 5 to 10 will be reinstalled from the date of completion. Note: All directions in this navigation notice start from 0 degrees north, rotating clockwise to 359 degrees, except for light directions, which are calculated from the sea. Light intensity is based on clear weather, and fog signals are only used in foggy weather. Further explanations will be provided if necessary. Depth measurements are calculated based on the datum plane used in the largest-scale chart.

County Government Announces Deed Tax Rates 146

The Shanghai County Government previously received an order from the province to reduce the field and housing deed tax from May of this year to six-tenths for sales and three-tenths for mortgages on a trial basis for three months. Together with the surtaxes approved for collection in this county, all will be reduced according to this example. This has been announced and communicated to all district and township offices for unified notification. Now, in order to ensure that the public understands the tax rates, the amounts of various regular and surtaxes to be collected during the reduction period were listed in a public notice yesterday for general knowledge. The details are as follows: Under the sales deed tax item, the regular tax is 6 yuan per 100 yuan of the deed price, plus a self-government surtax of 6 jiao 6 fen li, a construction surtax of 6 jiao 6 fen 6 li, a party affairs surtax of 6 jiao 6 fen 6 li, a regular tax collection fee of 5 li, and a handling fee of 3 jiao. The total for each 100 yuan of sales deed price is 8 yuan 2 jiao 9 fen 8 li. Under the mortgage deed tax item, the regular tax is 3 yuan per 100 yuan of the deed price, plus a self-government surtax of 2 jiao 5 fen, a construction surtax of 2 jiao 5 fen, a regular tax collection fee of 5 li, and a handling fee of 1 jiao 5 fen. The total for each 100 yuan of mortgage deed price is 3 yuan 6 jiao 5 fen.

Northern Changsheng Public Association, Rumors of Selling Public Property Denied, Reorganization Committee Publishes Clarification 151

The Northern Changsheng Public Association on Tangshan Road in this city was founded during the Xianfeng period of the Qing Dynasty, and it has been more than seventy years now. It is a charitable and public welfare organization with a well-established reputation in this city. Because most of the members of the public association have scattered in all directions in recent years, making it almost impossible to count them, the city party headquarters instructed eleven members of the public association, including Xu Shanchang, Jiang Fuchen, and Zhang Baofu, to reorganize the association on January 21 of this year. All public property is currently being kept in the care of members of the reorganization committee. Recently, there have been rumors that the public association is selling its property and that the members will share the proceeds, causing members to inquire about the truth and even a few to come to the association to collect money.

It is reported that the reorganization committee of the public association has submitted a report on the situation to the Ministry of the Interior and other relevant agencies for record and explanation, and has published a clarification notice in major newspapers in this city to clarify the truth.

Twenty-Four Tobacco Merchants Request Tax Rate Changes, Tax Office Refutes Tobacco Merchants' Statistical Errors 152

According to the Guowen News Agency, since twenty-four manufacturers, including the Chinese tobacco factory merchants and the public in this city, requested the improvement of the cigarette tax rate, the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance has prepared an audit explanation for this case, criticizing the errors in the numbers cited by the Public and other companies, and advising tobacco merchants not to be misled by tax reductions and to focus on developing their business. The original text of the explanation is found as follows:

Regarding the matter of the Public and twenty-four other companies requesting the revision of the cigarette tax tiers, their petition was directly submitted to this department. Later, the proposal by Huang Ziping, representative of the Public, and the review opinions of the Cigarette Association's General Assembly were transferred to the department by the Cigarette Association. Overall, the original petition requested a revision of the tiers, mentioning only that the seven-tier system was most beneficial to Chinese merchants, without proposing any specific plan. However, its tax tier calculation table advocated a three-tier system and set 80 yuan as the low-tier tax amount. Its main opinions on the number of tiers were contradictory. The subsequent proposal suddenly made a different claim, stating that the low-tier tax of 80 yuan could be changed. The main purpose of the proposal was no less than a request for tax reduction, which was very different from the original petition's purpose of equal treatment and revision of the tax tiers. As for the review opinions of the Tax System Review Committee of the General Assembly of Members, it merely expanded and explained the claims made in the original petition and proposal, without proposing any concrete plan for improving the tax tiers that could be considered. The statistics adopted in the original petition and the two documents were unfortunately not clearly researched. Now, the more important claims are specifically listed, audited together, and explained in sequence below. (Items listed in the original petition that are also mentioned in the proposal and review opinions are mainly based on the original petition and summarized for auditing to avoid repetition.) (1) The original petition listed errors in the time of the opening and revision of the cigarette consolidated tax. The original petition stated that the cigarette consolidated tax was opened in 1929 and revised three times in November 1930, February 1931, and March 1932. The seven-tier tax era lasted from July 1929 to November 1930, the old three-tier era lasted from November 1930 to February 1931, the new three-tier tax era lasted from February 1931 to March 1932, and the two-tier tax era has lasted from March 1932 to the present. This department's investigation shows that the cigarette consolidated tax was opened in February 1928 and revised five times in December 1928, October 1930, February 1931, March 1932, and November 1933. The old seven-tier era lasted from February 1928 to November, the new seven-tier era lasted from December 1928 to September 1930, the old three-tier era lasted from October 1930 to January 1931, the new three-tier era lasted from February 1931 to March 20, 1932, the old two-tier era lasted from March 21, 1932 to December 4, 1933, and the new two-tier era has lasted from December 5, 1933 to the present. (2) The original petition's description of the number of Chinese merchant bankruptcies is untrue. The original petition stated that there were a total of 150 to 160 Chinese merchants in the seven-tier tax era, but they closed down one after another during the two-tier tax era, and now only 40 to 50 remain. This department's investigation shows that there are two types of cigarette merchant organizations: one is a merchant with a machine factory, commonly known as a cigarette factory, and the other is a merchant that does not have a factory and entrusts another factory to roll the cigarettes, commonly known as a cigarette company or cigarette shop. According to the archives, 87 cigarette factories paid taxes and purchased flowers in 1931, and 90 did not have a machine factory but entrusted another factory to roll the cigarettes, totaling 177. Also in 1932, there were 83 cigarette factories and 44 that did not have a factory but entrusted another factory to roll the cigarettes, totaling 139. Therefore, comparing the total number of merchants paying taxes for the three years, the number has consistently been around 140, with cigarette factories accounting for 80 to 90, maintaining a balance. There is no truth to the original petition's claim that there were 150 to 160 and now only 40 to 50 remain. (3) The original petition's explanation and appended comparison table of British and American sales of stamps and tax payment table both contain errors. Regarding the explanation of the sales of stamps, the original petition stated that the average number of stamps sold by British and American companies in the three-tier tax era was 30,472, while other companies sold 68,422. The quantity of cigarettes sold by British and American companies was only 40% of that of other companies, less than 50%. In the two-tier tax era, the average number of stamps sold by British and American companies was 48,808, while other companies sold 44,323. The quantity of cigarettes sold by British and American companies has exceeded that of other companies by 485. Regarding the explanation of the number of tax payments, the original petition stated that the average number for British and American cigarette companies in the three-tier tax era was 2,417,403.822, while other cigarette companies paid 206,252.647. The British and American companies' burden was 410,000 more than that of Chinese merchants. In the two-tier tax era, the average number for British and American cigarette companies was 2,726,392.522, while other cigarette companies paid 2,554,466.996. The British and American companies' burden was only 170,000 more than that of Chinese merchants. The petitioners based their explanations on the above and separately created a comparison table of the sales of cigarette consolidated tax stamps and a comparison table of tax payments for British and American cigarette companies and other cigarette companies in the three-tier and two-tier tax eras. This department has carefully reviewed the original gazettes and stamp tax account books and found four errors in the statistics used in the original petition regarding the stamp table. (1) The original petition did not examine the actual situation of stamp sales at the time. From the opening of the cigarette consolidated tax to February 1932, the stamps of the former Cigarette Consolidated Tax Office or the former Consolidated Tax Department were sold in two places: one at the Coupon Fund Committee and the other at the former Cigarette Tax Office or the former Consolidated Tax Department. The table of British and American cigarette companies' sales of stamps by grade published in the former Consolidated Tax Gazette refers to the number of stamps purchased by the companies from the Fund Committee. The table of other cigarette companies' sales of stamps by grade refers to the number of stamps sold by the former Consolidated Tax Department. The tax amount listed in the tax payment table in the gazette is also divided into British and American (Column A, the value of flowers purchased from the former Consolidated Tax Department, British and American (Column B, the value of flowers purchased from the Fund Committee). At the time, this was noted monthly in the tax payment table's annotation column. The tax amount listed in the British and American (Column B) of the tax payment table must be equal to the total in the value column of the table of British and American sales of stamps by grade. The two tables can be mutually verified. (For example, in the tax payment table in the January 1931 Consolidated Tax Gazette, the British and American (Column B) counted 1,716,901.250 yuan as the number of flowers purchased by British and American companies from the Fund Committee, which is equal to the total in the value column of the table of British and American sales of stamps by grade, 1,716,901.250 yuan.) Therefore, the number listed in the other companies column in the stamp table compiled by the original petitioners still contains a portion of British and American purchases, totaling 8,934 first-grade stamps (including 1 old third-grade stamp), 37,3397 second-grade stamps, and 306,006 third-grade stamps (including 1,652 old third-grade stamps), for a total of 344,239.1 new and old stamps, equivalent to a tax amount of 15,219,592.7 jiao. The original petition adopted statistics without inquiring clearly beforehand, leading to erroneous one-sided conclusions and incorrect citations. (Attached is a table of British and American purchases of flowers at the department from January 1931 to February 1932.) (2) In February 1931 and March 1932, old tax stamps were returned due to tax rate revisions and should be deducted accordingly. The original petition did not pay attention to this during calculation. (3) March 1932 was a transitional period between the old and new taxes. The number of new and old stamps should have been listed separately to reflect the actual situation. The original petition omitted March, which is not appropriate. (4) Stamps should be calculated according to their face value by tax grade to match the actual tax revenue. The original petition did not distinguish grades or convert tax rates into tax amounts for mutual verification with the tax amount table, inevitably leading to misunderstandings. (For example, in the original stamp table, British and American companies had 24,560 stamps in June, while the tax amount table shows 2,048.629 yuan. However, according to the actual situation, the number of stamps should be divided into 60 first-grade stamps, 2,500 second-grade stamps, and 22,000 third-grade stamps, equivalent to a tax amount of 1,078.8009.) The original petition also made four errors in the tax amount table. (1) The face value of the old tax stamps returned by merchants at the time of the above-mentioned tax revisions was deducted in the tax amount table, but the number was not deducted in the stamp table, so the utility of comparing and verifying stamps and tax amounts was lost, and it was difficult to obtain the true picture from the statistics. (2) The tax amount listed in the former Consolidated Tax Gazette included the cigar tax, which the original petition did not clearly account for. (3) Since imported cigarettes changed to collecting the full amount of the gold unit customs duty in November 1931, all consolidated taxes were waived, but the customs still allocated four-fifths of the collected customs duty to the department monthly. The original tax amount still included this allocation from imports, which should be excluded to reflect the true picture of tax payments from domestically produced cigarettes. The original petition also failed to examine this. (4) During the three-tier tax era, imported goods were stored in warehouses until the two-tier tax was implemented, when they were subject to supplementary tax before leaving the factory, and other supplementary tax issues arose. The supplementary tax collected was recorded in the total tax amount. This supplementary tax was not included in the number of first-grade stamps sold at the time and should also be excluded. However, the original petition uniformly considered it to be the tax amount for domestically produced cigarettes, which is confusing. Based on the above points, the original stamp comparison table and tax amount comparison table have been corrected and recompiled separately with explanations to clarify the truth. Attached are the corrected detailed table of cigarette stamp grades and the cigarette tax revenue trial calculation table for the three-tier and two-tier tax eras. Also, the three-tier tax period lasted for fifteen months. For the convenience of statistical comparison, the number of months for the two-tier tax is also taken as fifteen. (To be continued)

Shanghai Gentlemen Wang Xiaolai, etc., Initiate the Reconstruction of the Cao E Filial Daughter Temple 153

According to the Shenshi News Agency, the filial daughter Cao E was from Shangyu, Kuaiji. Her father, named Yan, was skilled in stringed instruments and singing and was a shaman. On the fifth day of the fifth month of the second year of Han An (the reign of Emperor Shun of Han), he drowned while praying to welcome the gods. Cao E was fourteen years old and cried along the river for seventeen days before jumping into the river and dying. After several days, she floated out with her father's corpse in her arms. Nine years later, the county magistrate Du Shang reburied her and Han Zhan Chun wrote a wonderful epitaph to record the miracle. In the first year of the Han Yuanjia era, a temple was built by the river to honor the filial daughter. Zhu E of the Song Dynasty and Zhu E of the Ming Dynasty were worshiped continuously in all dynasties. In the tenth year of Qianlong of the Qing Dynasty, the temple was once destroyed by fire, but only the rear hall was affected. On July 19, 1929, the entire temple was burned down, becoming scorched earth. The old yellow silk tablet from two thousand years ago was destroyed in an instant, and there was no one to rewrite it like Cai Bian, which is a shame to the ancients. Now Shanghai and Zhejiang gentlemen and merchants Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Qin Runqing, Yu Zuoting, Wang Zhengying, etc., have initiated the reconstruction of the Filial Daughter Temple as a plan to revive traditional morality and have established a preparatory committee, issued donation books, and are raising funds from all walks of life. It is hoped that during this period when the New Life Movement is sweeping the country, there will be enthusiastic donations to support and protect the typical figures in history, and that alms will be collected to accomplish this great undertaking.

The Society for the Protection of Animals Requests a Ban on Cruelty to Living Beings 170

The Chinese Society for the Protection of Animals, noting that there are often cruel acts inflicted on innocent animals in the market, such as suffocating pigeons with small coin pouches, cutting the tongues of pheasants to kill them, breaking the tails of snails, hanging chickens and ducks upside down, and skinning frogs, etc., points out that such behavior was previously prohibited by the Shanghai Mixed Court, with offenders being fined. Using innocent animals as food is already inappropriate, and to cause them more pain before death is even more unbearable for the benevolent. They have specifically sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, requesting that they issue a ban in accordance with the previous Shanghai Mixed Court's ban on cruelty to living beings, in order to protect living beings and curb cruelty.

A Domestic Helper Dies Tragically from Abortion at a Westerner's Home; The Paramour Flees Without a Trace; The Doctor is Still Under Investigation 171

Fang Zhang, a woman from Hangzhou, 39 years old, residing at 162 Hart Road, was widowed. Zhang was quite romantic and worked as a domestic helper in a Westerner's home. Unaccustomed to living alone, she had an affair with someone, and after repeated clandestine meetings, she became pregnant. Recently, in order to save face, Ms. Zhang intended to remove the fetus, so she hired a doctor to perform an abortion. Unexpectedly, although the fetus was removed from the abdomen, she fell ill and her condition worsened day by day. A few days ago, she was taken to Guangren Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and she died shortly after. The hospital reported to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, which ordered detectives to investigate. It was learned that the man had fled without a trace, and the female doctor who performed the abortion was from Fahua Town in Shanghai West. She first gave Ms. Zhang medicine and then performed surgery. Since the detectives knew that the female doctor lived in the Chinese area, they were unable to investigate. The Sixth District Public Security Bureau has been notified to investigate. The body was taken to the forensic examination office on Philemon Road. Zhang, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, accompanied by a forensic doctor, arrived at the office to examine the body. Shou Tianxi testified that he was 35 years old, from Hangzhou, and had been living in his hometown as a merchant. He learned of the matter and came to Shanghai, temporarily residing at the home of a friend at 231 Xinyili, Morling Road. The deceased was his uncle's wife. She had been working as a domestic helper in a Westerner's home in Shanghai. Her husband had already passed away and she had several children. He did not know the rest of the details. Since none of her family members were here, he requested permission to claim the body. Prosecutor Zhang accepted the testimony and ordered an examination, which determined that the deceased, Fang Zhang, died of peritonitis caused by an abortion. The body was handed over to Shou Tianxi to be taken back for burial.

Shocking News

Detectives Divide Stolen Money and Rape the Woman in the Case, Lu Yang; The Entire Case is Transferred to the District Court After Discovery - Rickshaw Pullers and Others Fined Separately for Encroachment 172

Rickshaw puller Wang Baokang once pulled a cashier from a money shop who lost 5,000 yuan in cancelled banknotes. Wang took them home and hid them under a box at the bottom of his bed. Later, he took the money to buy new clothes, which was noticed by his landlord, Meng Guopei, who suspected that Wang had owed rent for several months, so where did he get the money to buy clothes? In the evening, he peeped through a crack in the board and saw Wang counting the bills, all of which were cancelled banknotes. He remained silent and secretly stole several hundred yuan the next day. Wang returned home and found out, causing a great commotion. The news spread, and Wang's usual loan sharks and creditors from his gambling days also arrived. Wang knew things were not good, so he repaid his debts and distributed dozens of yuan to each person. Those who received this benefit included Meng Guopei, Wang Jinkui, Wang Qixian, Wang Li, Zhou Wang, and Lu Yang. Wang knew that the matter had been publicized and was dangerous, so he took the money and fled back to Jiangbei, living the life of a small rich man. However, the news gradually leaked out due to the large number of people involved and was learned by the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau. Meng was arrested and confessed the reason, so detectives Sun Shucheng, Zhang Yuzhuo, Zhou Wenhai, and Yang Zhongjin were sent to Jiangbei to arrest Wang Baokang and others. However, the detectives used their authority to seize the stolen money and divide it among themselves, and raped Lu Yang. After arriving in Shanghai, the case was investigated in the Third Division of the Public Security Bureau. Due to many flaws in the handling of the case, after strict questioning of the defendants, this shocking and absurd incident was discovered. Therefore, the detectives were detained and sent to the District Court for public prosecution. Yesterday, Judge Zhang sentenced them all to minor punishments. Wang Baokang was fined 200 yuan for encroachment and 50 yuan for gambling, totaling 220 yuan. Meng Guopei and Wang Jinkui were each fined 80 yuan for receiving stolen goods. Wang Qixian was fined 90 yuan for receiving stolen goods and gambling. Sun Shucheng was sentenced to six months of imprisonment for encroachment. Zhang Yuzhuo, Zhou Wenhai, and Yang Zhongjin were each sentenced to three months of imprisonment. Wang Li, Zhou Wang, and Lu Yang were not guilty because they were women.

A Horrible Incident

A Russian Commits Suicide While Drunk, Yimalef was in the Hat Business, A Bullet to the Temple, He Died Instantly 173

In room 2 on the second floor of the Western-style apartment building at 847 Avenue Joffre in the French Concession lived Yimalef, a White Russian traveler, 46 years old, who was in the hat business. He was addicted to alcohol, and most of his income was spent on it. Yimalef also had a natural bad habit, that is, he must drink when he sees alcohol, he must get drunk after drinking, and he must cause trouble after getting drunk. His wife, Al Zhaomiler (48 years old), often advised him, but Yimalef still drank heavily as usual, without any repentance, which often caused disputes between the couple. Yesterday at about 4:15 PM, Yimalef was drinking again, and as a result, he was drunk and didn't know what he was doing. He suddenly felt a sense of being in a foreign land and of family discord. He suddenly had the idea of committing suicide, and hid in the kitchen alone, opened a pistol and committed suicide. The first bullet grazed his left forehead, and the second bullet hit his right temple, killing him instantly. His wife heard the sound and rushed over, but Yimalef had already fallen in a pool of blood. She immediately reported to the police station. The police chief immediately sent Chinese and Western detectives to investigate and then sent the body to the forensic examination office on Taras Road, waiting for the court to send someone to examine it.

The Contribution of the United Premium Company - A New Strategy for Developing Industry and Commerce 174

The United Premium Co., Ltd. was initiated by prominent figures in this city and organized in accordance with the provisions of the Company Law of the Co., Ltd., and has been approved for registration by the Ministry of Industry and issued a license No. 662. After the company was established, it set up an office on the third floor of 110 Sichuan Road in order to save time and realize its goals as soon as possible, so that all sectors could enjoy its benefits, and actively proceeded. It hired lawyer Liu Shifang as its legal advisor and accountant Xu Yongzuo as its auditor. On the one hand, given that this type of business has been popular in Europe and the United States for many years and has achieved remarkable results, people in those countries have believed that it is the only good strategy to promote business to increase sales of existing goods and to gain a position for new goods. However, in China, this is the first of its kind. In order to improve, a special commissioner was sent to the United States for detailed investigation, and the results of the investigation have been sent to Shanghai. The opening is near, around mid-July. The details are summarized below:

Business 175

The company's business, the greatest goal, is to assist merchants and develop business. Because today all industries are in recession and the public's purchasing power is shrinking, it is necessary to supplement excellent quality and fair prices with premiums. Then the public will not receive unexpected benefits, and manufacturers can increase business, benefit each other, and adjust each other, so that the market can be restored to prosperity. However, the current premium methods are carried out independently and have no strong appeal or considerable interest. Now the company specially prints joint premium coupons and sells them to manufacturers for joint application, attaching them to goods to be given away. Those who get the coupons can accumulate a certain amount and exchange them for various premiums they like at the premium exchange offices set up by the company. Because of the ease of getting the coupons, the variety of premiums, and the intense interest, and careful calculation, this is a great cost-saving method. This method is popular in Europe and the United States, and adopters have benefited three times over. For example, the Winterford Company in the United States increased its business by as much as 81 percent by using this premium coupon. Now the company's approach is roughly similar to that of the United States' greatest joint profit-sharing company, but it also fits the current social situation in China and is enough to solve the difficulties of merchants. Therefore, if handled properly, success can be assured.

Premiums 176

The premiums used by the company are mainly novel and practical. All are ordered from major famous factories. More than 700 types have been selected by the company, and the selection is still in progress. In the future, there will be a dazzling array, which is predictable.

Exchange Office 177

The company's premium exchange office in this city is attached to the Guangshi Company on Nanjing Road. In other places, it is handled by branches of the China Travel Service, including Nanjing, Suzhou, Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Xuzhou, Hankou, Tianjin, Peiping, Qingdao, Jinan, Bengbu, Wuhu, Jiujiang, Changsha, Zhengzhou, Jinchang, Hangzhou, Quanhua, Guangzhou, and Kaifeng, etc. Later, it will also add to the places in succession in order to seek popularization. In places outside this city where there is no premium exchange office, coupon holders can exchange premiums by mail to the Shanghai General Management Office of the company.

Catalog 178

In order to make the public understand the premium exchange method and various premiums, the company will print 500,000 copies of the premium catalog for widespread distribution.

Instructions 179

The company has printed a book entitled "How to Promote Sales and Develop Business" for merchants to understand the company's business and the advantages of joint premiums. Merchants can write to the company for a copy, which will be sent immediately.
