Shen Bao Medical Weekly

Elaborating on Typhoid Fever (1) 278

— Yu Yunxiu

Those who discuss typhoid fever invariably follow Zhang Zhongjing's Treatise on Cold Damage. And those who discuss the Treatise on Cold Damage cannot escape the Six Channels. In my view, the most meaningless aspect of the Treatise on Cold Damage is the Six Channels. The most preposterous aspect is the theory of the Six Channels. What are the Six Channels? Taiyang, Shaoyang, Yangming, Taiyin, Shaoyin, Jueyin. Their names first appeared in the Inner Canon's Twelve Meridians and Twelve Tendon Meridians. The meaning of their names all originated from the words of shamans and diviners. The Treatise on Absolute Essentials from the Simple Questions states: "The Emperor asked, 'What is Yangming?'" Qi Bo replied, "It is the merging of the two Yangs." The Emperor asked, "What is Jueyin?" Qi Bo replied, "It is the complete intersection of the two Yins." The Spiritual Pivot's Yin-Yang Relationship with the Sun and Moon chapter explains its meaning in detail. It states: "Yin signifies the birth of Yang in the first month. It governs the Shaoyang of the left foot. Wei signifies the sixth month. It governs the Shaoyang of the right foot. Mao signifies the second month. It governs the Taiyang of the left foot. Wu signifies the fifth month. It governs the Taiyang of the right foot. Chen signifies the third month. It governs the Yangming of the left foot. Si signifies the fourth month. It governs the Yangming of the right foot. These two Yangs combine in front, hence the name Yangming. Shen signifies the birth of Yin in the seventh month. It governs the Shaoyin of the right foot. Chou signifies the twelfth month. It governs the Shaoyin of the left foot. You signifies the eighth month. It governs the Taiyin of the right foot. Zi signifies the eleventh month. It governs the Taiyin of the left foot. Xu signifies the ninth month. It governs the Jueyin of the right foot. Hai signifies the tenth month. It governs the Jueyin of the left foot. These two Yins intersect completely, hence the name Jueyin." Ma XuanTai commented: "Taking the first, second, fifth, and sixth months as Shaoyang and Taiyang, with the third and fourth months residing within, these two Yangs combine and illuminate in front, hence the name Yangming. Taking the seventh and eighth months as the initial birth of Yin, and the eleventh and twelfth months as the initial birth of Yang, only the ninth and tenth months represent the end of Yin, hence the name Jueyin." Thus, what is referred to as Tai, Shao, etc., designates the first month as Shaoyang, the second month as Taiyang, the third month as Yangming, the sixth month as Shaoyang, the fifth month as Taiyang, the fourth month as Yangming, the seventh month as Shaoyin, the eighth month as Taiyin, the ninth month as Jueyin, the twelfth month as Shaoyin, the eleventh month as Taiyin, and the tenth month as Jueyin. However, examining the Apocryphal Texts of the Book of Changes, the winter solstice is considered the middle of the eleventh month, corresponding to the Taiyin of the foot, which aligns with the eleventh month Taiyin in the Spiritual Pivot. Lesser Cold is considered the solar term of the twelfth month, corresponding to the Taiyin of the hand, which does not align with the twelfth month Shaoyin in the Spiritual Pivot. Greater Cold is considered the middle of the twelfth month, corresponding to the Shaoyin of the foot, which aligns with the twelfth month Shaoyin in the Spiritual Pivot. Beginning of Spring is considered the solar term of the first month, corresponding to the Shaoyang of the foot, which aligns with the first month Shaoyang in the Spiritual Pivot. Rain Water is considered the solar term of the first month, corresponding to the Shaoyang of the hand, which aligns with the first month Shaoyang in the Spiritual Pivot. However, Zheng commented that it should correspond to the Taiyang of the hand in terms of the meridian, which does not align with the Spiritual Pivot. Startling of Insects is considered the solar term of the second month, corresponding to the Taiyang of the foot, which aligns with the second month and Yang in the Spiritual Pivot. Spring Equinox is considered the middle of the second month, corresponding to the Taiyang of the hand, which aligns with the second month Taiyang in the Spiritual Pivot. Pure Brightness is considered the solar term of the third month, corresponding to the Yangming of the foot, which aligns with the third month Yangming in the Spiritual Pivot. Grain Rain is considered the middle of the third month, corresponding to the Yangming of the foot, which aligns with the third month Yangming in the Spiritual Pivot. Beginning of Summer is considered the solar term of the fourth month, corresponding to the Yangming of the hand, which aligns with the fourth month Yangming in the Spiritual Pivot. Lesser Fullness is considered the middle of the fourth month, corresponding to the Taiyang of the foot, which does not align with the fourth month Yangming in the Spiritual Pivot. Grain in Ear is considered the solar term of the fifth month, corresponding to the Taiyang of the foot, which aligns with the fifth month Taiyang in the Spiritual Pivot. Summer Solstice is said to be the middle of the fifth month, corresponding to the Yang pulse of the hand. According to the example of the Spiritual Pivot, it should be Taiyang. However, the allocation in the Apocryphal Texts of the Book of Changes does not entirely align with the Spiritual Pivot. Therefore, what is referred to as the Yang pulse, it is unknown which Yang it refers to. Lesser Heat is considered the solar term of the sixth month, corresponding to the Yangming of the foot, which does not align with the sixth month Shaoyang in the Spiritual Pivot. Greater Heat is considered the middle of the sixth month, corresponding to the Shaoyang of the hand, which aligns with the sixth month Shaoyang in the Spiritual Pivot. Beginning of Autumn is considered the solar term of the seventh month, corresponding to the Shaoyang of the foot, which does not align with the seventh month Shaoyin in the Spiritual Pivot. End of Heat is considered the middle of the seventh month, corresponding to the Taiyin of the hand, which does not align with the seventh month Shaoyin in the Spiritual Pivot. White Dew is considered the solar term of the eighth month, corresponding to the Taiyin of the foot, which aligns with the eighth month Taiyin in the Spiritual Pivot. Autumn Equinox is considered the middle of the eighth month, corresponding to the Shaoyang of the hand, which does not align with the eighth month Taiyin in the Spiritual Pivot. Cold Dew is considered the solar term of the ninth month, corresponding to the Jueyin of the foot, which aligns with the ninth month Jueyin in the Spiritual Pivot. Frost's Descent is considered the middle of the ninth month, corresponding to the Jueyin of the foot, which aligns with the ninth month Jueyin in the Spiritual Pivot. Beginning of Winter is considered the solar term of the tenth month, corresponding to the Shaoyang of the hand, which does not align with the tenth month Jueyin in the Spiritual Pivot. Lesser Snow is considered the middle of the tenth month, corresponding to the Pericardium meridian. The Pericardium is the Jueyin of the hand, which aligns with the tenth month Jueyin in the Spiritual Pivot. Greater Snow is considered the solar term of the eleventh month, corresponding to the Hand Pericardium, which does not align with the eleventh month Taiyin in the Spiritual Pivot. This discusses things in terms of the value of the month. Its reasoning has no root, and its numbers are all different. It can be known that it cannot be relied upon.

Dedicated to Young and Future Mothers (4) 279

— Guo Dashi

Under these circumstances, cod liver oil, calcium, vitamins, and exposure to sunlight can be applied for a considerable amount of time in order to allow the baby's bones to develop adequately.

XXXXX

In terms of various senses, the infant's sense of taste develops earliest, and they understand the condition of the food that passes through their mouths first. Therefore, mothers should be careful about things that infants can easily get their hands on and should not give sharp objects to children to play with.

The infant's sense of hearing is not fully developed. After two months, we sometimes see the infant's head turning in the direction of the sound.

A baby, if healthy, will begin to smile after two months. Between six and eight months, we can hear the infant's babbling sounds. Between nine and ten months, they will be able to call out "Papa! Mama!" These are the words that adults are looking forward to hearing. Once they pass their first birthday, they will be able to recognize words.

By the age of two, the infant's ability to speak has developed considerably. At this point, parents should no longer speak to them in childish "baby talk," but should speak formally to make it easier for the children to forget their incomprehensible "baby talk."

I know that every infant's mother wants to know about teething, so I will write down what we have personally observed here:

The average infant sprouts their first tooth in the sixth month, and then one tooth each month thereafter, so that by the second year they should have twenty teeth.

At this time, calcium should be prepared in the infant's diet.

Infants should have adequate exercise every day. Because legitimate exercise not only makes breathing easier and increases digestive power, but also helps development, corrects posture, and achieves good movement.

Infants can begin indoor gymnastics after four months. Mothers should try to make their children interested in gymnastics, singing songs or doing other movements while performing gymnastics.

The duration of gymnastics should initially be only five minutes, gradually increasing to fifteen minutes.

Gymnastics must not be performed just before or shortly after meals, otherwise it will consume digestive power.

During gymnastics, the infant must be awake and not too hungry. In short, the most important thing is to have a set time, and to put clothes on him immediately after the exercise so that he does not catch a cold.

Before starting gymnastics, it is best to consult a doctor and get his guidance.

XXXXX

Finally, I want to make mothers aware of some of the laws they should know in case of unexpected dangers to their little darlings.

If a mother finds that her child is very uncomfortable, she should first put him in bed and then measure his temperature.

If the temperature is very high, a cloth (or towel) soaked in hot water can be wrapped around the upper body, which will be effective.

Sometimes the infant's throat should also be noted, as many diseases often arise from there. Cuts or other minor injuries to the skin should be dabbed with iodine and then wrapped in a bandage. In case of burns, use lime water or cottonseed oil to wrap.

In the case of cramps or convulsions, first lay the child down, and then cover the head and chest with a cold cloth.

In case of foreign objects being swallowed by the child,

or getting into the ears or nose, a doctor should be consulted immediately.

I hope that the above opinions and methods will at least be of some use and help to young and future parents. (The End)

Note: "Kilocalorie" is a medical term for measuring heat.

Regarding "Ideal Medical Association" Response to Mr. Pang and Mr. Chen 280

— Song Guobin

Since I published the article "Ideal Medical Association" in this journal, Mr. Pang Jingzhou provided "further interpretation" of my humble article, and Mr. Chen Fangzhi even added a stern "review." I, being ignorant and simple-minded, have not been able to deeply understand the ways of the world. I believe that the lack of progress in the Chinese medical community in recent years is due to the divergent opinions of various factions. A medical association is an organization that represents the entire medical community, and what is called the national general medical association is like the central government of a country. A government cannot have two, so how can a medical association have three? Therefore, I advocated the union of the three associations in order to achieve the effect of unified authority. When power can be concentrated, it will naturally have more than enough resources to deal with internal and external affairs. I speak from the heart, and there is no so-called background. Moreover, since it is called "ideal," it is not yet certain whether it will become a reality. Although I have been practicing medicine for many years, I seem to have done nothing more than teach and treat patients. Therefore, I dare not claim to be able to understand the inside story of the medical community deeply. What I know, others also know. And as for the three major medical associations, I have no relationship with them whatsoever, and I am in a different field than those who manage them. Therefore, I dare to take the position of a fourth party, represent the opinions of ordinary colleagues, and publish the article "Ideal Medical Association." "Without desires, one is firm," as the ancient saying goes. The merits of my humble opinion are to be judged by the public, but I am deeply confident in my "desirelessness." Now, after reading Mr. Pang's article, I realize that what I said only followed the popular view, that there are no factions within the medical community, and that unity is not difficult. Therefore, I was overjoyed and knew that my previous belief that unity was not easy was just a杞人憂天杞人憂天's worry. Before I could finish celebrating, Mr. Chen's article came out. After repeatedly reading it, I realized that not only are there divisions between factions within the medical community, but also that opinions are like fire and water, and that unity will never be possible. Then, I could not help but feel sad and know that those who have been working hard for unity are like the Foolish Old Man moving mountains. The mountain cannot be moved, but if you insist on moving it, this is why the Wise Old Man of Hebei laughed and left. Mr. Chen is a senior in the medical community and has been in politics for many years. Using his experience in politics, he infers the situation of the medical community. Seeing that the political situation has not been unified in the past 20 years, he anticipates that the medical community cannot be united. This kind of insight is different from those of us who only know the superficial aspects. Therefore, he expressed his honest opinion and enlightened me. This is what I should thank Mr. Chen for. As for saying that what I said seems to have a background, and that the idea of unity is equal to eliminating dissidents, I am a pure doctor, with no political skills and no factions to speak of. Then what do I love and hate, that I must flatter one party and make enemies with another? This is what I want to declare to Mr. Chen.

Common Sense Q&A About Diseases 281

— Cheng Hanzhang

(29) Epidemic Dysentery

(Question) What is epidemic dysentery?

(Answer) It is a dangerous diarrheal disease that specifically attacks children aged three to six during the summer and autumn.

Page 16

(Question) What is its cause?

(Answer) The cause is unclear, but it seems to be similar to dysentery bacteria or E. coli.

(Question) Why are children susceptible to epidemic dysentery?

(Answer) The contributing factors are eating indigestible fruits and candies, drinking excessive cold drinks, and being exposed to cold while sleeping at night.

(Question) Why is this disease dangerous?

(Answer) Because epidemic dysentery can cause severe toxic symptoms in sick children.

(Question) After infection, before the onset of the disease, is there an incubation period?

(Answer) There is an incubation period of several hours to twenty-four hours.

(Question) What are the initial symptoms of the disease?

(Answer) The child suddenly loses strength, becomes inactive, and lies quietly.

(Question) What are the symptoms when the disease breaks out?

(Answer) The body temperature rises (fever) to 38 to 39 degrees Celsius: at the same time, two or three foul-smelling soft stools or diarrhea are discharged. The stool contains undigested matter and mucus. Soon, the body temperature rises further to 40 to 41 degrees. The nature of the stool is mucus and blood, without tenesmus (straining) or feeling of incomplete evacuation, and it can occur dozens of times a day. In addition, vomiting may occur at the onset, with brownish or coffee-ground-like substances being vomited. The stool also contains black things. These are all from bleeding in the digestive tract that has turned black.

(Question) What are the abdominal symptoms?

(Answer) The child's abdomen is slightly sunken, soft, and often has abdominal sounds and tenderness to the touch.

(Question) What other symptoms are there?

(Answer) Other symptoms include drowsiness, convulsions, rapid and weak pulse, pale skin, cold limbs, and a pale face, leading to death.

(Question) How long does the most severe stage last?

(Answer) The most severe stage lasts twelve to twenty-four hours, leading to death from cardiac paralysis.

(Question) What happens in milder cases?

(Answer) In milder cases, the body temperature drops within one or two days, and various symptoms gradually disappear, leading to recovery.

(Question) Are there even milder cases?

(Answer) There are also cases where there are only a few episodes of diarrhea, a mild fever, or the discharge of a few stools containing mucus, and then it stops. These symptoms resemble ordinary gastroenteritis.

(Question) How is it diagnosed?

(Answer) Whenever a child suddenly loses strength, is tired, and lies down, this disease should be suspected. If there is a high fever, vomiting, toxic symptoms, mucus in the stool, but no tenesmus, then this disease can definitely be diagnosed.

(Question) What is the degree of danger after the prognosis?

(Answer) The younger the age, the more dangerous it is. Obese children are worse off than thin children. The mortality rate is twenty to thirty percent.

(Question) What is the treatment for epidemic dysentery?

(Answer) It is the same as for ordinary dysentery. Special attention should be paid to the heart, and cardiotonics are often used. If there are toxic symptoms, physiological saline, etc., must be injected.

(Question) What are the preventive measures?

(Answer) They are the same as for dysentery, which is to disinfect the patient's feces and prohibit the consumption of uncooked, indigestible, and unclean food. Pay attention to the cleanliness of drinks, etc.

The Treatment of Leprosy 282

— Gao Mingqiang

The International Leprosy Conference was held in Manila, Philippines, on January 9, 1931. Most of the participants were experienced physicians from various countries engaged in leprosy work, totaling more than twenty people. The conference lasted for two weeks, which was an unprecedented grand event in the medical field. All the resolutions were published in the Philippine Journal of Science. Subsequently, the Wood Memorial Fund for the Eradication of Leprosy in New York printed one thousand copies and distributed them to major medical organizations around the world. This article is translated from the chapter on treatment in the conference's resolution report. I hope readers will not treat it lightly. —Translator

The treatment of leprosy must be carried out with both general therapy and specific therapy in order to be effective. Moreover, these therapies must vary according to each individual patient and cannot be applied uniformly.

(1) General Therapy The general therapy for leprosy is roughly similar to that used for other chronic infectious diseases. However, most physicians with experience in this disease believe that diseases that impair resistance must be avoided by leprosy patients as much as possible, which is an important key to effective treatment. Furthermore, proper management of the quality and quantity of food is also quite important. Other factors such as personal hygiene, appropriate exercise, mental well-being, and light work all have considerable value in treatment and should not be overlooked.

(2) Specific Therapy All procedures concerning treatment and attempts to eliminate disease areas can be called specific therapy, such as the application of drugs and surgery.

The most widely used drug is chaulmoogra oil and its various preparations. The most commonly used oils are named Hydnoocarpus Wightiana and H. anthelmintioa (both of which belong to the chaulmoogra family and are the best of this class). Among the preparations of these oils, the most noteworthy for treatment are the ethyl esters and sodium salts of fatty acids. From a clinical point of view, these oils and their various preparations are almost identical in therapeutic value. Therefore, the choice of application mostly focuses on ease of acquisition, convenience of transportation, purity of quality, and permanence of preservation.

Ethyl esters are widely used in major treatment centers and are favored by those engaged in leprosy treatment everywhere. The reason for this is that the manufacturing process of this drug enables each product to be fixed, uniform, and have a certain standard. Moreover, the lack of local reaction during injection is superior to other preparations. Furthermore, this reaction can be reduced by adding five parts per thousand of iodine. Some physicians prefer to use pure oil and sodium salts of fatty acids. Although these drugs can be used for intramuscular or subcutaneous injection, the effect of intradermal injection is not as good as ethyl esters, so it is rarely tried.

Injection methods include intramuscular, subcutaneous, intradermal, and intravenous. The method of selection should be determined by the nature of the drug. For example, pure oil is not suitable for intradermal injection, and ethyl esters are better; and pure oil and ethyl esters are not suitable for intravenous injection, etc., all of which must be paid attention to. Moreover, skin lesions can often be easily dissipated by intradermal injection. As for the amount of various drugs used, there is no fixed standard and it must be determined according to the patient's tolerance.

There are also several other Hydnocarpus-like oil agents used. However, the experience gained is not yet sufficient to evaluate its value.

In order to facilitate the patient's recovery, controllable febrile reactions are often adopted. Physical therapies such as ultraviolet light, radiant heat, and hot baths are all very beneficial to leprosy patients.

Other drugs such as gold preparations and other heavy metal preparations have also been tried, but must be very careful. Iodides are not very suitable for most patients. Based on experience, this type of drug can only be used for patients who are physically strong and have a high tolerance for chaulmoogra-like preparations.

Standards for Treatment and Assessment It is not yet time to obtain a standard treatment method at present. The most satisfying method is intradermal injection of Hydnoocarpus oils. At the same time, it can be used in combination with intramuscular injection. Leprosy is a chronic disease, so the effectiveness of the methods and drugs used in treatment must be determined one or several years after application. Moreover, there is currently no accurate method to assess the value of treatment. Clinical and microscopic examinations are often erroneous and cannot be performed without skilled surgery, trained personnel, and careful examination.

On the Treatment of Syphilis (Can 606, 914 Completely Cure Syphilis?) (Part Two) 283

— Shen Gong

(3) Bismuth preparations. The application of bismuth in the treatment of syphilis began in recent years. However, it is mostly used as an auxiliary drug in combination therapy rather than used alone. Compared with the efficacy of arsenic, bismuth, and mercury, various reports are inconsistent.

Arsenic nine: Bismuth seven: Mercury five (Frieboes)

Arsenic ten: Bismuth seven: Mercury four (Milian)

Arsenic ten: Bismuth six: Mercury four (Gougerot)

However, Brocq said that the efficacy of bismuth is not greater than that of mercury.

(4) Iodine preparations. Iodine preparations are weakly effective in the first stage of syphilis. However, in the later stage, the effect is quite large. Iodine preparations only take effect after being decomposed in the body. There are also two methods of administration: injection and oral administration. However, side effects are also unavoidable.

Drugs can cure diseases, but they can also kill people. Therefore, proper handling is the dividing point between medical skills. The question of whether syphilis can be completely cured is still controversial and there is no consensus. In short, if patients can receive appropriate treatment early, the results will be fast and sure. Therefore, the issue of seeking medical attention after being infected with syphilis is quite different. The application of drugs is valuable in that it has a hierarchy. For example, in the first stage of syphilis, the main treatment is injection of arsenic preparations, combined with bismuth preparations or mercury therapy. In the second stage, mercury or bismuth preparations should be used first. After two or three weeks, arsenic preparations should be injected again. In the third stage, iodine preparations can be used to remove rashes. However, complete treatment also relies on arsenic, bismuth, and mercury preparations. In patients with internal organ or neurosyphilis, treatment with iodine, bismuth, and mercury should be done first. Then, arsenic preparations can be injected slowly. Therefore, patients often think that they have been cured after ten injections. In fact, there is often regret that they want to be fast but fail to achieve it. Curing diseases is valuable in that it treats the root cause. If only the appearance is taken into account, it will turn out to be a clumsy attempt and lead to so-called latent syphilis. Latent syphilis means that there are no signs of syphilis on the outside, but the blood still shows a positive reaction. If more people suffer from latent syphilis, there will be more opportunities for heredity. And the number of congenital syphilis patients will also increase accordingly. The treatment is more troublesome and not as straightforward as in the early stage after infection. At this time, the world is in recession, and the Chinese people are especially poor. Under the difficulties of food and clothing, the number of people who cannot receive appropriate treatment is countless. There are also occasional wealthy families who are confused by advertisements and misled by quack doctors. This is because they only know the properties of 606 and 914 drugs, but do not know the situation after the drug properties enter the body. Nowadays, doctors often use people's psychology to use their stupidity to lure patients by using a quick cure as bait. Those who are deceived by them do not realize it in the end. It is lamentable. Here, I cannot help but loudly shout that syphilis should first pay attention to prevention. Second, a setback therapy should be performed early. Third, long-term combination therapy must be received. Woe to this sight full of sores. Do not be confused by the false claims of the world.

A Brief Discussion of Pulmonary Tuberculosis (5) 284

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 3: Inducing Factors for the Occurrence of Tuberculosis

Now that tuberculosis bacteria have reached the trachea or lungs, does that mean that pulmonary tuberculosis will immediately develop? This is also not certain. The formation of ordinary pulmonary tuberculosis involves two conditions. The first is the "external cause," which is how tuberculosis bacteria invade the human body, as mentioned in the transmission routes above. The second is the inducing factor. What is meant by an inducing factor? We must understand that each person's physical adaptation status is different: in other words, the degree of resistance is different for everyone. As mentioned in the airborne transmission above, tuberculosis bacteria can invade the human body anytime and anywhere when they are scattered in the dust in the air: so no matter who it is, one or two tuberculosis bacteria always enter the trachea in a day. In this case, wouldn't everyone become a pulmonary tuberculosis patient? But in fact, it will never be like this. Ordinary healthy people have resistance to eliminate invading bacteria: even if the bacteria are unfortunately successful, sometimes only minor local changes occur, and not everyone spreads into a disease, forming what is generally called (clinically provable) the disease itself. But if the body is weak, the resistance is weak, and there are congenital and acquired defects, then it is of course not the same as the former and it is easy to form. This easy-to-form state is the "inducing factor" presented in this chapter. What are the inducing factors of pulmonary tuberculosis? The most important of these is of course what is commonly called the consumptive constitution. People who have this kind of constitution are generally: narrow face, long neck, narrow chest, ribs sloping downward, deep hollows in the supraclavicular fossa, slender hands and feet, and poor development of muscles and fat. His appearance is weak, his complexion is pale, his teeth are neat, his inspiratory muscles are weak, and his heart and vascular system are easily excited. Such a physique is very easy to develop tuberculosis. The reason for this is mostly congenital.

The apex of the lung is also the easiest place to form tuberculosis infection. Because the respiratory movement of the apex of the lung is relatively weak, and its gas exchange is less than that of other parts of the lung: if tuberculosis bacteria and dust reach the apex of the lung, it is difficult to remove them from there. In addition, the blood supply to the apex of the lung is also less than that of other parts of the lung. This situation is very beneficial for the formation and progression of tuberculosis. Whether or not pulmonary tuberculosis is easily formed is also related to age. Generally, the number of cases is highest in those over eighteen and under thirty: there are also many children. In those over forty, there are relatively fewer cases, and even if there are, the progression of the disease is mostly chronic. But in the elderly around sixty years old, obvious cases are also quite a few. In terms of gender statistics, there are more men than women, which is of course because there are more opportunities for contact infection.

Regarding people's environment, place of residence, place of work, past acute illnesses, and various chronic diseases; all of these are very related to the occurrence of pulmonary tuberculosis. Like living in a humid place where sunlight and air do not circulate, working in a closed factory all day long, and in dirty air: or because of the backward economic situation, the three meals a day are not complete, and the lack of nutritious food is even more likely. These situations can all promote the formation of pulmonary tuberculosis. In terms of disease, diseases such as diabetes, typhoid fever, whooping cough, measles, chronic bronchitis, and bronchopneumonia can all weaken people's body resistance: and of course, they are also a great help to the occurrence or progression of pulmonary tuberculosis. Regarding congenital pulmonary artery stenosis and blood loss from the lungs, these two conditions can also be regarded as inducing factors for tuberculosis. But I think the reason for this is too biased towards academic theory and cannot be understood by people who have not studied medicine, so I will not discuss it here. (End of this chapter, to be continued)

Correction of the Name of Cholera 285

— Song Guobin

The name "Zhendan" originated from Buddhist books, and the name "Zhina" originated from Japan. In essence, they all refer to China, but the Chinese people use them without careful consideration. They use foreign transliterations to replace our original characters. Therefore, saying "stupa" for pagoda and "bhikkhu" for monk is already the case in ancient books and cannot be changed. However, it is not as bad as it is in modern times.

Since the eastward transmission of Western culture, new medicine has become increasingly developed, causing a huge shock. As a result, many medical terms have been transliterated, but their errors are quite alarming. Some deviate in pronunciation, and some deviate in meaning. They follow foreign translations without asking what the true meaning is. Scholars advocate it, and the common people agree with it. For decades, no one has realized it. Although the government has reviewed and approved it, the errors still persist after the review and approval. It is assumed that since it has been used for a long time, it has become a habit, and it is inconvenient to change it once. Then how can there be a revolutionary spirit? If, although it has been reviewed and approved, this has not been seen, then the reviewers are also difficult to exonerate from the responsibility of acting hastily! In the past, I once said that the character "jia" in thyroid should be changed to "dun." "Jia" is armor, and "dun" is a weapon for defending against soldiers. To say "dun" is to deeply understand its shape, and to say "jia" is to have no direction to point to. The Japanese say that "dun" is "jia," so it is not an error to use it. In our country, "jia" and "dun" are already distinguished, so their shapes are different. Continuing to use it without changing it is a great mistake! As for typhoid, it is the transliteration of the Western name Typhus Abdom. The Japanese read "zhi" as "chi," so it matches the pronunciation. Our country reads "zhi" as "zhi su qie," which is a deviation in pronunciation. It is only because the Japanese translated it first, and we follow it later, without any independent opinion, and we say what others say. This is why Japan wants to have China. I have examined the disease "cholera." It originated in Asia. The English, French, and German countries all call cholera Cholera. The Japanese medical community translates the sound of Cholera as "torareera," and the etymology of the word Cholera has not yet been determined. Some say it comes from Greek, meaning "bile flow" or "ditch diarrhea," and some say it comes from Latin, meaning "evil disease." There are various opinions, and there is no consensus. What is certain is that it is not an ancient European term.

What is even more advanced is that the three names "cholera" and "torareera" have different characters, but their pronunciations are actually similar. Since the original character of torareera is Cholera, then the word Cholera seems to be undoubtedly the transliteration of cholera. Therefore, when it comes to the source of the disease, it was born in East Asia, and when it comes to the ancestor of the term, it came from China. Now, we abandon the established name containing meaning and follow the Japanese translation that has sound but no meaning, translating each other, and the true meaning is completely lost. Our Chinese people have intensified and abbreviated it as "tiger plague," as if there is a so-called big insect plague in addition to rat plague. Nothing is more laughable than this. The new generation of scholars know the name of torareera but do not know cholera. Is this not what is called forgetting one's ancestors? If the slave nature is not changed, independence is difficult to achieve. Medical terms are the most trivial, but the expression of a spirit of worshiping foreigners is already complete! Correcting it is also the responsibility of those who care about the world and people's hearts. What do you gentlemen of the world think?
