Amateur Mailbox

National Salvation Through Simple Clothing 307

Editor:

"Can the slogan 'National Salvation Through Simple Clothing' save the country?" Several years ago (in 1918 and 1932), I had already started this movement. At that time, because I was still an apprentice who had not completed his apprenticeship, my knowledge was shallow and my strength was weak, and I could not persuade people all over the country, which was a great regret. What I advocated at that time was all to my confidants, such as "relatives," "friends," and "clansmen," etc. Of course, the effect was limited. Now, at this time of national crisis, my regret has been aroused again, so I am writing this letter to ask you.

(1) How should it be communicated to the whole country so that everyone buys domestic cotton cloth?

(2) It is easy to implement this method in rural villages (because of their frugality), but it is difficult to implement in prosperous cities such as "Shanghai," "Hankou," and "Nanjing." What method can be improved and made easier to implement?

(3) How to stop the sales of foreign cloth? What is the reason for its sale?

(4) How deep is this problem for the interests of the country?

(5) Why can't Chinese native cloth be consumed by most people?

(6) How to encourage the public's enthusiasm to buy native cloth?

(7) Why is the production of cotton in China, which has a wide land, so scarce? What method can be used to encourage the villagers to improve and increase the harvest so that the factory does not use foreign cotton?

Please give your best guidance on the above issues, which will not only benefit the country, but also slightly activate the people's economy. When I am doing business at the counter now, I also publicize my views and persuade farmers not to buy foreign cloth. Foreign cloth is not as durable, strong, and economical as Chinese cloth. Although I am persuading them so painstakingly, I don't know if God can make me achieve my wish? Sincerely wish you

Xu Zhuyou

Answer: Many of the questions you asked are repetitive, so I will answer them all together. There are many slogans for saving the country, such as "Saving the country by reading" and "Saving the country by aviation," etc. "Saving the country by simple clothing" is just one of these slogans. The purpose of advocating "saving the country by simple clothing" is nothing more than two things: promoting the virtue of frugality and developing the national economy. What you pay attention to is the latter, and now we will discuss the meaning of the latter.

A hundred years ago, we would never have had this slogan. We all wore native cloth at that time, but as a result of wearing native cloth, our country was not saved, but fell into a more miserable fate. The reason for advocating native cloth now is that more and more people are using "foreign cloth" and fewer and fewer people are using "domestic cloth." Therefore, if we want to make people buy native cloth, we must make "foreign cloth" not be bought or used by anyone in China. The reason why foreign goods are dumped in China is nothing more than two things: good quality and low price, and foreign goods have various privileges in China and are not subject to harsh taxes. Therefore, if we want to develop our country's national economy, or more specifically, revitalize our country's industry, or more practically, have the people all use their own goods to avoid the outflow of interests, we should cancel the conditions for foreign goods to be dumped in China. Foreign cloth is of good quality and low price, and our domestic cloth is of better quality and lower price. Increase the tariff rate to raise the cost of foreign goods, and at the same time abolish harsh taxes to lower the price of domestic cloth. In this way, is there any reason why domestic cloth will not sell well? Is there any reason why anyone would want to buy foreign cloth?

The editor is very respectful to all those who are determined to save the country, but he is often not satisfied with the means he takes. The motivation of those who advocate "saving the country by simple clothing" is very pure, but this kind of movement may not be put into practice, and its effect may not be beneficial to the national economy and the people's livelihood. If people are poor, they will wear native cloth even if they don't save the country. On the other hand, if they are encouraged by patriotism to wear native cloth, they will not be able to last in the end. Even if it can last, it will not save the country. Many farmers in the countryside wear "native cloth," but the country is not saved because they wear native cloth. On the contrary, they themselves are extremely poor and need the country to save them. By analogy, everyone wears "simple clothes," but everyone is poor, and the country becomes a "simple clothing country," but it is often subject to the oppression of imperialists. In this way, what salvation have the "country" and the "people" gained? Leaving aside the purpose, just in terms of realization, the two effective methods we mentioned earlier for making people use "domestic cloth" instead of "foreign cloth" will definitely not be put into practice under the current situation. Abolishing the privileges enjoyed by foreigners in China or asking for higher tariffs, how dare ordinary timid people like carp raise these demands to foreign countries? Of course, making things with good quality and low price themselves can resist foreign goods. However, comparing the economic structure of our country today with those of other countries in the world, this is also impossible.

Therefore, we know that to save China, it is not possible to achieve results by patching up bit by bit. The only way we can save China is to remove all the shackles that imperialists have placed on China, that is, to "abolish all unequal treaties" as mentioned in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will.

As for how to achieve this, the editor believes that we can only achieve our goal by firmly holding the attitude of preferring to be shattered like jade rather than surviving like a tile, and by dealing with the imperialists. Editor

Notice to Mr. Huang, please send the Grand Hotel magazine for verification, Supplement Editing Room

Novel

The Poor Gentleman (12) 308

— By English writer George Gissing, translated by Sun Pu

Mr. Dymond was not versed in psychology. But he immediately and very clearly saw the moral crisis he had been living through. Moreover, the question of poverty once again taught him a truth.

After breakfast, he immediately went downstairs and knocked on Mr. Shag's office door. "What is it?" the bookbinder asked, his mouth full as he ate his fourth piece of bacon.

"Sir, I would like to request a leave of absence for an hour or two this morning. There is something important that I need to do."

Mr. Shag replied with the elegance befitting a man of his type, "I suppose you can go ahead and do as you please. I wasn't paying you any salary anyway."

The speaker bowed and withdrew.

Two days later, he wrote another letter to Mrs. Weale. The letter read as follows:

"The money you so kindly sent, which I have received, has now been distributed. To ensure the proper use of these funds, I have entrusted the cheque and a clear statement of its intended use to a local pastor. He has kindly included a list of the beneficiaries' names in an attached letter, which I believe will satisfy you.

"But, you will ask me, why did I seek the help of the pastor? Why do I not, based on my own experience, aid the poor people in whom I have a personal interest? Why is this pleasure not given to myself -- I, the man dedicated to a mission of mercy?

"The answer is both simple and clear. I have lied to you.

"I do not live in this place of my own free will. I am not dedicated to charitable work. I am merely – no, no, I WAS – a poor gentleman who, at one time, because of a foolish speculation, lost his fortune and, ashamed to explain this to his friends, fled into an unfortunate life of seclusion. You see, I have added shame to misfortune. I do not wish to tell you how close I came to doing something bad.

"I have learned a skill, which I believe will supplement my meagre income and allow me to live a better life than before. If possible, I ask you to forgive me and forget me henceforth.

Your tedious S.T. Dymond"

Film Special

Monday, May 21st, 1934, The Shun Pao Screen Section

Why Stars Cannot Be Mothers (Part 2) 309

— Guang Dao

Hollywood's Declining Productivity

A Star's Motherhood Means Sacrificing a Career

The first person we must mention is, of course, Gloria Swanson, known as a 'good mother'. She has been married several times, but marriage has not hindered her career. Later, because of her intense love for children but her reluctance to give birth herself, she adopted several children, which did not affect her career. It wasn't until she still felt empty and had to have her own children that her career suffered a great blow. Becoming a mother herself meant losing her status as a star. Although she struggled desperately to return to the screen, her hardship was even greater than when she worked hard as a swimmer in the past. Recently, although she has won the sympathy of the film industry, and her former employer MGM has given her a contract, it is feared that this is merely an expression of MGM's sympathy for an aging actress. Norma Shearer is always mentioned as an actress whose motherhood was not enough to ruin her future. But let us examine this more closely. She is indeed a big star - with stunning beauty, a distinct personality, and a talent for acting. She also married a powerful film entrepreneur, Irving Thalberg - who was also doing his best to help her fight to return to the screen. However, how does her career compare to before she became a mother? The film she starred in after giving birth was A Free Soul, but that film did her no good. That film made Clark Gable, Lionel Barrymore, and Leslie Howard even more famous, while Norma Shearer remained the same, with no progress. Although her looks have not aged, her artistry has not diminished, she works hard herself, and she has a powerful husband to help her, it will probably be extremely difficult for her to regain her former position as a first-rate leading actress. Let's take another example, Helen Twelvetrees. Several years ago, she gave up her film career to have a child. At that time, she was in a top role, earning $2,700 a week. But she gave it up lightly. She originally thought that she could have a child, rest for a few months, and then return to the screen. She did not know that she was taking a great risk. So, after she had her child and recovered her health, she found that her status as a star had dropped to that of an ordinary actress. And she had to start all over again. Because of the difficulty of finding work, she had to take on small roles for small salaries. She said: 'I want to prove that my abilities have not diminished at all, so I have to work hard.' It is true that her abilities have not been lost at all, but the film industry changes in an instant. In the few months that she was giving birth, the world was no longer the world it used to be.

There are countless examples like this. Bebe Daniels is also one of them. There is no need to mention other less famous actresses. Some people say that if an actress has children before becoming famous, her children will not necessarily affect her status. For example, Marlene Dietrich, before she became famous, already had Maria. But she never dared to let her daughter meet the audience in 'The Scarlet Empress'. Later, although she allowed her daughter to show her face in that film, she was still somewhat uneasy about the result. She is indeed a very careful person. (End)

Film Reviews

Review of "The House on 56th Street" - Da Guangming Theater 310

— Ling He

Based on past observations and experience, we believe this is a very marketable work. After watching it, the playwright grabs the audience's sympathy with a sentimental sophistry, and the Chinese audience is relatively easy to accept the atmosphere of tragedy.

Moreover, the clear and understandable narrative method from beginning to end makes it relatively easy for people to understand.

I think that most people will not deny that this is a thoroughly sentimental work. Of course, some explanation must be added to the nature of sentimentality. The sentimentality of 'Storm in a Teacup' damaged and even destroyed the enthusiasm for progress. Therefore, the sentimental method should be abandoned by progressive writers; for the sake of a powerful emphasis on the effect of the play. Then how should we explain the use of this sentimental method of writing about the decadent lives of the upper classes? Perhaps some people will say; let us let them sigh at the sentimentality in their decline process, it has nothing to do with us. However, this reason is not entirely correct. When a clever author uses the emphasized sentimentality to make us sympathize with people we should not sympathize with, then this is the author's victory, but for the vulnerable audiences, it is a loss, although there is no poison of any degree in the work. I remember that Warner Bros.' son-in-law (i.e., Lorell, the director of 'The Story of Louis Pasteur') once said in an interview in Japan that the main feature of Warner Bros.' film production is the novelty of the story, and they even often ask many people to find script materials from newspapers and magazines. We can very well believe this statement from Lorell's mouth. Then the so-called twists and turns of the story of 'The House on 56th Street' are indeed not accidental. Indeed, on the surface, the story here is very bizarre and tortuous. Regarding this point, I think there is no need to copy the instruction manual to introduce it, anyway, people who have seen it will always admit it. However, precisely because it is intentionally made tortuous, it is organized using the method of sophistry. It is inevitable that there are not enough real places in the structure, and many overly idealized places write the dancer played by Claudette Colbert as a Superman. Naturally, we understand that the playwright is making the heroine Lily move upward. Under the interpretation of the old concept, she became a virtuous wife and mother from the life of a dancer. Although she has a hereditary love of gambling, and although she is proficient in gambling, she wants to work hard to be a good person, use her skills to teach her daughter not to gamble, and even do so for the gamblers. In this way, she became a Superman. She was imprisoned for twenty years on suspicion of murder, and later was willing to suffer for her daughter, although she was acquitted because of the political power of the gangster. What is even more obvious is that after accidentally meeting the gambler on the ship, she immediately repented and returned the money she had won to him, which is definitely not something that ordinary people can do. However, the playwright is always a sophist. In his creative methods, such small places will not be noticed. For example, he never lets the daughter know her mother, which increases the great tragic power. Naturally, the theme of this work is against gambling. And on the other hand, it also exposed the shortcomings of unclear laws. However, from the perspective of the protagonist's personality development, this is that the woman's fall does not have its inevitability. However, he sophistically raped the audience's emotions, and this person who should not be sympathized with finally made people sympathize. Speaking of sophistry and rape, of course we will not ignore Robert Florey, the French director who is now in China inspecting the exteriors of 'Oil Lamps'. He emphasized the sentimentality of the play using extremely skilled film techniques. The editing is economical, the narration is clear and smooth, no abuse of music, no trendy manufacture of gimmicks or exaggerations, and in the slightest, static sounds are used to increase the psychological changes of the people in the play, and the actors are fully allowed to develop their dramas. Sentimentality is everything in the play, and sentimentality is also the director's greatest victory. The protagonist Claudette Colbert played a role with the same sentiment as in 'Imitation of Life', but it was the highest achievement she has achieved in all the works she has starred in.

"The Show-Off" - Cathay Theater 311

This is an adaptation of George Kelly's comedy, which is light, funny, and contains some slight satire on life.

Most of the story is made up of coincidences, and the ending can be said to be unreasonable, but in the playwright's unintentional, it reflects a lot of satire on modern marriage problems, and slightly reveals some of the sorrows of the petty bourgeoisie. Of course, this is just an unintentional revelation and reflection.

A salary earner who is good at showing off his wealth but is actually poor marries the daughter of a real estate company owner by chance, but after marriage, his 'nature' is exposed, and he is 'greatly ridiculed by his in-laws', and 'the woman is extremely angry, and urges him to leave'. This is something that can be heard and seen every day. Later, after wandering and drifting around, he falls to the streets as a 'sandwich board man', which is what salary earners (especially those who like to show off) should encounter at this stage. However, American films certainly do not allow such a tragic ending, so as usual, they use one or two accidental opportunities to make him 'get lucky' and the couple reconcile. It is very clear that as long as the audience is a little sober, they can know that such 'good luck' is rare, and such couples often cannot 'reconcile'.

The places that reflect the reality of society are very touching, such as being ridiculed by the mother-in-law and ridiculed by the wife, etc. However, those places about 'good luck' inevitably make people feel that they are acting. Spencer Tracy's good acting is worth seeing.

Audience Opinion

Watching "Two Against One" 312

— Hou Yuhong

Because the Star Company values this film too much, it spares no effort to go all out. The actresses include Xuan Jinglin, Gao Qingping, Ai Xia, etc., and the actors include Gong Jianong, Zheng Xiaoqiu, Wang Zhengxin, etc., but the facts tell us that this 'Two Against One' has not achieved more excellent results because of so many excellent actors. The reason is that the story is too scattered and the meaning is too vague. The director cannot get the center of directing the progress, and the actors cannot grasp the goal of expressing emotions. Therefore, except for dancing, singing, and drinking champagne, it can be said that there is nothing. This is what we deeply regret!

The individual expressions of the actors, Gong Jianong and Wang Zhengxin are better, and the actresses have no emotions to speak of. The two ball games lack tension because of too many splicing problems. But why does the Star Company want to go all out to perform such a superficial script? In addition to feeling that there is no drama to perform, I am afraid it is also to avoid the demands of the directors.

Movie Novel

Wonder Bar (4) 313

— Shu Ming

When Yvette ran into Al's office, Harry had already taken the five thousand dollars and left. Yvette didn't know and still wanted Al to find a way to stop Harry from leaving. Al told her that Harry had just taken the five thousand dollars. When Yvette heard this, she jumped up and made a big scene with him. She scolded him. She said, 'I always thought of you as a friend, but it turns out you are so heartless!' Al let her make a scene because he knew very well that what he did was entirely for Yvette and he had done nothing wrong. Moreover, he himself deeply loved her. Now that Harry had left, he could slowly find a way to make her forget about Harry. While Yvette was making a fuss, Li suddenly ran in. He told Al that Harry was going to run away with Mrs. Renard. Al didn't believe it and said, 'Are you crazy!' Li snorted and said, 'Am I crazy? They just broke up. I was watching her. She later sneaked out through the side door and went to Harry's car. She is still waiting for Harry in the car, waiting for him to finish his performance before leaving.' Yvette was stunned and couldn't speak for a moment. Al was furious and said, 'To abduct the wife of one of the most powerful men in Paris! This is how he repays me! My hotel is going to be ruined!'

Al immediately went outside the side door and found Harry's car. He took a flashlight and shone it into the car and sure enough, he saw Mrs. Renard curled up. He said, 'Mrs. Renard, a thousand apologies. Someone told me that you went to the wrong car. You went to someone else's car.' The beautiful Liane said, 'That's right, but thank you for being so careful. My husband and I are going home with the owner of this car.' Al said, 'Great. I'll go tell Mr. Renard that you're waiting here.'

Liane hurriedly stopped him and said, 'No, no, he'll come himself.' Al had a change of heart and thought that he had to change his strategy. He said, 'Mrs. Renard, when can we be frank with each other?' Mrs. Renard pretended not to understand and said, 'What frankness?' Al then said very calmly, 'You have to understand that your husband is a close friend of mine and often takes care of my hotel. If I let his wife do something wrong, he will definitely blame me, understand?' Liane said angrily, 'I don't understand!' Al then warned her very solemnly, 'If you leave here with Harry, you will regret it for the rest of your life!' Liane said angrily, 'How dare you--come and talk to me like that!' Al touched his pocket and said slowly, 'I have the guts, but not as big as Harry's. Do you know where Harry got the money to run away with you?' Liane couldn't speak for a moment. Al then took out the diamond necklace and showed it to her and said, 'He sold me your necklace.' After he finished speaking, he put the necklace in her hand and said, 'This is a small gift from me, please accept it, madam.' Liane grabbed Al's hand. She got out of the car and walked back into the ballroom with Al. Harry and Yvette had just taken the stage to perform the whip dance. Yvette stood solemnly at the door of the ballroom, listening to the music of her whip dance, preparing to take the stage. She was inserting a sharp knife into her garter. The knife was originally an accessory in the whip dance. A moment later, the two of them took the stage and the atmosphere in the entire hall was extremely tense. (To be continued)
